- [[guanyinzi-chapter-two|Guanyinzi Chapter Two / 關尹子第二章]] — Chapter Two of the Daoist classic Guanyinzi explores the cosmological principles of establishing heaven and earth through all things, the interplay of essence, spirit, and the five elements.
- [[guarding-practices-wenzi-guardianship|Guarding Practices (守) in Wenzi / 文子"守"系列哲學]] — The ten "Guarding" practices in Wenzi Volume 3 represent a comprehensive Daoist self-cultivation methodology, including guarding emptiness, non-being, equilibrium, simplicity, clarity, authenticity, stillness, law, weakness, and plainness.
- [[guarding-stillness-wenzi-jing|Guarding Stillness (守靜) in Wenzi / 文子"守靜"論]] — Guarding Stillness (守靜) in Wenzi Volume 3 presents stillness as the fundamental governance principle, contrasting it with chaos caused by movement, and emphasizing its role in preserving spiritual energy and achieving longevity.
- [[heart-death-zhuangzi|Heart Death / 心死]] — The Zhuangzi concept that spiritual death (heart death) is greater than physical death, representing loss of true nature and spontaneity.
- [[huaxu-dream-liezi|The Huaxu Dream (華胥之夢) / 華胥之夢]] — The Yellow Emperor's dream journey to the utopian land of Huaxu, representing ideal governance and natural harmony.
- [[hun-tun-chaos-death-zhuangzi|The Death of Hun-tun (渾沌之死) / 渾沌之死]] — The parable in Zhuangzi where well-intentioned intervention by 儵 and 忽 destroys the natural simplicity of 渾沌, illustrating the dangers of artificial interference with natural states.
- [[jian-de-zhi-guo|Nation of Established Virtue / 建德之國]] — The ideal Daoist society described by Shi Nan Yi Liao in the Zhuangzi—simple, without artificial desires, where people act freely and live and die with peace.
- [[kangcangzi-ear-vision-eye-hearing|Kangcangzi: Seeing with Ears and Hearing with Eyes / 亢倉子·耳視目聽]] — A Daoist sage who transcended ordinary sensory limitations through spiritual cultivation, described as able to see with ears and hear with eyes.
- [[kun-peng-giant-fish-bird-liezi|Kun and Peng / 鯤鵬]] — The legendary giant fish Kun that transforms into the massive Peng bird, a cosmological concept from Liezi describing the vastness of the universe and the transformation of beings.
- [[non-attachment-guanyinzi|Non-Attachment (無物) in Guanyinzi / 關尹子之無物論]] — The Guanyinzi's doctrine of non-attachment to things (無物), emphasizing that the sage responds to the world without grasping and nurtures the self without ego.
- [[shan-mu-yi-dai-niao|The Yi Dai Bird / 意怠鳥]] — The story of the humble, non-competitive Yi Dai bird in Zhuangzi's Mountain Trees chapter, illustrating the Daoist path of safety through humility and non-distinction.
- [[sheng-ren-zhi-dao-sages-way|The Sage's Way / 聖人之道]] — The philosophical principle from Guanyinzi chapter 3 describing how the sage governs through naturalness, humility, and selflessness rather than through personal intervention.
- [[the-lost-sheep-at-the-crossroads|The Lost Sheep at the Crossroads / 歧路亡羊]] — A philosophical parable illustrating how multiple paths lead to loss, emphasizing the importance of unified focus in learning and practice.
- [[xiang-tian-shu-he-xiang-tian-shu-zhi-jian|Natural Affinity versus Interest-Based Relationships / 相天屬與相利合]] — A philosophical contrast in Zhuangzi between relationships formed through natural bonds versus those formed through mutual benefit.
- [[xing-hai-nei-wai|Inside and Outside the Physical Form / 形骸內外]] — A philosophical distinction in Zhuangzi between the physical body (form) and inner virtue, exemplified by deformed sages whose outer appearance differs from their inner perfection.
- [[xu-ji-yi-you-shi|Swimming Through the World with an Empty Self / 虛己以遊世]] — A Zhuangzi parable about how one who empties oneself of ego and self-interest becomes invulnerable to external harm.
- [[zhuangzi-daozhi-chapter|Robber Zhi Chapter (盜跖) / 盜跖篇]] — Zhuangzi Chapter 29 presents a fictional dialogue between Confucius and Robber Zhi, featuring radical critiques of Confucian morality, civilization, and social order.
- [[zhuangzi-true-painter-anti-art|The True Painter / 眞正的畫者]] — The Zhuangzi story of a painter who achieved perfect spontaneity by removing all conscious thought, embodying Daoist non-action in artistic creation.

## Category:Governance

- [[analects-zhengzhi|Governance in the Analects / 论语中的治理]] — Examination of Confucius' principles of governance as outlined in the Analects.
- [[de-dao-zhe-duo-zhu-shi-dao-zhe-gua-zhu|De Dao Zhe Duo Zhu, Shi Dao Zhe Gua Zhu / 得道者多助，失道者寡助]] — The Mencian principle that a ruler who follows the Way (Dao) will receive abundant assistance, while one who abandons it will have few supporters, establishing moral legitimacy as the foundation of political power.
- [[five-priorities-governance-daxizhuan|The Five Priorities of Governance in Daxizhuan / 禮記大傳人道五端]] — The Daxizhuan chapter of the Book of Rites outlines five governance priorities:亲近、报功、举贤、使能、存爱, forming the foundation of Confucian political philosophy.
- [[governance-leadership|Governance and Leadership / 治理与领导]] — Analyzes the principles of governance and leadership in the context of Confucian ethics, focusing on the responsibilities and virtues of leaders.
- [[mengzi-hegemon-true-king-ba-wang-distinction|Hegemon versus True King (霸道與王道) / 霸道與王道]] — Mencius's distinction between rulers who govern through force (hegemon) and those who rule through virtue (true king).
- [[mengzi-people-heart-minjian|The People's Heart / 民心]] — Mencius' doctrine that legitimate governance depends on winning the hearts of the people through benevolent rule.
- [[mengzi-unity-through-non-killing-ding-yu-yi|Unity Through Non-Killing / 定於一]] — Mencius' doctrine that unity of the realm is achieved through rulers who do not delight in killing.
- [[mozi-honoring-worthy-three-standards|Honoring the Worthy with Three Standards / 尚賢三本]] — Mozi's doctrine emphasizing the selection of virtuous officials based on three essential standards: rank, salary, and authority.
- [[mozi-worthy-historians-emperors|Wise Ministers of History / 聖賢履歴]] — Historical examples of unworthy individuals rising to power through virtue, as cited in Mozi's Honor the Worthy chapter.
- [[providing-people-sustenance-zhi-min-zhi-chan|Providing the People with Sustenance (制民之產) / 民に産業を制する]] — Mencius argued that benevolent government requires establishing the people's material welfare first—providing land, livestock, and education—because only those with stable livelihoods can develop constant virtue, making economic security the foundation of moral governance.
- [[ruo-min-weakening-the-people|Weakening the People (弱民) / 弱民]] — A Legalist political doctrine advocating that rulers should deliberately weaken the populace to strengthen state power, creating dependence through poverty and labor.
- [[san-lue-three-strategies|Three Strategies / 三略]] — A classical Chinese military treatise divided into three volumes (Upper, Middle, Lower) addressing military command, statecraft, and governance principles.
- [[shang-jun-shu-reward-punishment-system|Reward and Punishment System in Shangjunshu / 商君書賞罰制度]] — The Shangjunshu articulates a systematic framework of rewards and punishments as the primary instruments of state governance and military effectiveness.
- [[shang-xing-rewards-punishments|Unified Rewards and Punishment (賞刑) / 賞刑統一]] — Shang Yang's doctrine of unified rewards, unified punishments, and unified education as the three pillars of Legalist governance.
- [[shared-joy-with-the-people-yu-min-xie-le|Shared Joy with the People (與民偕樂) / 民と偕に楽む]] — Mencius's principle that rulers should share enjoyment with the people, not hoard pleasures for themselves.
- [[three-eras-san世-shangjunshu|Three Eras Theory / 三世說]] — The Three Eras Theory (三世說) from the Book of Lord Shang describes the historical progression of governance from primitive kinship society through aristocratic rule to centralized legal governance.
- [[tian-shi-di-li-ren-he|Tian Shi Bu Ru Di Li, Di Li Bu Ru Ren He / 天時不如地利，地利不如人和]] — The Mencian doctrine that favorable timing is less important than geographical advantage, which is less important than human harmony.
- [[tian-xia-you-da-zun-san|Three Universally Honored Things / 天下有三尊]] — Mencius's doctrine that there are three things universally honored in the world: rank (position), age (seniority), and virtue (moral character), with implications for the hierarchy of honor in governance and society.
- [[using-war-to-end-war-shangjunshu-doctrine|Using War to End War / 以戰去戰]] — Shang Yang's dialectical doctrine that war, when conducted properly, serves to eliminate the necessity of future warfare through establishing lasting dominance.
- [[wang-dao-true-king-hegemon|The Way of the True King vs. Hegemony (王道與霸道) / 王道と霸道]] — Mencius's distinction between righteous rule through virtue and coercive rule through force.

## Category:Liezi

- [[cicada-catcher-concentration-liezi|The Cicada Catcher: Mastery Through Focused Concentration / 痀僂承蜩：至精至專之道]] — The story of the hunchbacked cicada catcher demonstrates how absolute focus and singleness of purpose (用志不分) enables extraordinary skill in Daoist self-cultivation.
- [[dream-reality-confusion-liezi|Confusion of Dreams and Reality / 夢覺不分 / 夢と現実の混同]] — The Liezi philosophical anecdotes exploring the boundary between dreams and waking life, including the servant who dreamed of kingship and the firewood collector's deer.
- [[eight-testings-six-omens-liezi|Eight Testings and Six Omens / 覺有八徵夢有六候 / 八徵と六候]] — The Liezi philosophical framework classifying eight experiential states of waking life and six categories of dreams, with implications for understanding consciousness.
- [[huaxu-kingdom-liezi|The Huaxu Kingdom / 華胥氏之國]] — The Yellow Emperor's dream of the utopian Huaxu Kingdom and his subsequent enlightened reign, illustrating the Daoist ideal of natural governance through non-action.
- [[ji-shengzi-fighting-roosters-liezi|Ji Shengzi's Fighting Roosters: Spiritual Mastery / 紀渻子養鬭雞 — 精神修養之道]] — The story of Ji Shengzi cultivating fighting roosters illustrates the Daoist path to spiritual mastery through the progression from false confidence to true tranquility.
- [[king-mu-spiritual-flight-liezi|King Mu's Spiritual Flight / 周穆王神遊 / 周穆王のspirit journey]] — The philosophical discourse on spiritual transcendence as described in the Liezi account of King Mu's journey with the transformed person.
- [[laochengzi-illusion-transformation-liezi|Lao Chengzi's Study of Illusion / 老成子學幻 / 老成子の幻化学]] — The philosophical narrative of Lao Chengzi learning the art of transformation and illusion from Yin Wen, including the Daoist theory of change and the nature of reality.
- [[liang-xiao-er-bian-ri-two-children-sun-debate|Two Children Debating About the Sun / 兩小兒辯日]] — A famous anecdote from Liezi about two children debating whether the sun is closer in the morning or at noon, illustrating the limits of human knowledge.
- [[shangqiu-kai-faith-moves-heaven-earth-liezi|Shangqiu Kai: Faith That Moves Heaven and Earth / 商丘開：至信感人]] — The story of Shangqiu Kai demonstrates how supreme sincerity (至信) can move heaven and earth, allowing one to walk through fire without harm.
- [[yu-gong-yi-shan-yugong-moves-mountains|Yu Gong Moves the Mountains / 愚公移山]] — A famous Chinese fable from Liezi about an old man who decided to move two large mountains blocking his village, demonstrating the power of persistence and collective effort.

## Category:Mengzi

- [[mengzi-gaozi-debate|The Mencius-Gao Zi Debate on Human Nature / 孟子與告子之人性辯論]] — A philosophical exchange between Mencius and Gao Zi exploring whether human nature is morally neutral or inherently good.
- [[mengzi-gift-accepting-principles|Mengzi's Principles for Accepting or Refusing Gifts / 孟子不受无功之祿]] — Mencius's ethical framework distinguishing between acceptable gifts (travel provisions and security assistance) and unacceptable ones (gratuitous wealth that implies corruption), reflecting Confucian values on integrity and self-sufficiency.
- [[mengzi-losing-original-heart|Losing and Seeking the Original Heart / 放心]] — Mencius's concept of "fang xin" - the loss of one's innate moral consciousness and the imperative to recover it through learning.
- [[mengzi-righteousness-profit-debate|Mencius on Righteousness vs. Profit / 孟子论义利]] — Mencius' argument that rulers should be persuaded through benevolence and righteousness rather than profit, with profound implications for political philosophy.
- [[mengzi-ritual-food-debate|Mencius on Ritual Propriety vs. Necessity / 孟子论礼与食]] — The debate about whether ritual propriety or practical necessities like food and marriage take precedence, illustrating Confucian value hierarchies.
- [[mind-as-organ-of-thought|The Mind as the Organ of Thought / 心之官則思]] — Mencius's doctrine that the mind is the exclusive organ capable of moral reasoning, establishing the foundation for Confucian mental cultivation.
- [[ministerial-responsibility-resignation|Official's Duty and Right to Resign / 有官守者，不得其職則去]] — The Confucian principle that officials must resign when they cannot fulfill their duties or speak their mind.
- [[rites-food-debate-gaozi|The Debate on Rites versus Food / 礼与食孰重]] — The philosophical debate in Mencius about whether ceremonial rites (li) should take precedence over practical necessities like food and marriage, exploring the tension between moral principles and human needs.
- [[teaching-many-methods-mencius|Teaching Has Many Methods / 教亦多术]] — Mencius's pedagogical philosophy that不屑之教诲 (disdainful teaching) is itself a valid and effective method of moral education, representing a sophisticated understanding of educational psychology.
- [[willow-cup-metaphor-gaozi|Willow-Cup Metaphor / 杞柳桮棬]] — Gaozi's philosophical metaphor comparing human nature to willow wood that must be coerced into artificial forms, critiqued by Mencius.
- [[zhi-qing-relation|Will and Passion-Nature / 志與情的關係]] — Mencius's doctrine on the hierarchical yet interactive relationship between will (zhi) and passion-nature (qing)

## Category:Mozi

- [[fenyun-covered-siege-vehicle|Fenyun Covered Siege Vehicle / 轒轀]] — A heavily armored wheeled vehicle used in ancient Chinese siege warfare for crossing water obstacles and breaching defensive works, documented in Mozi's water defense chapter.
- [[mozi-banner-system-siege-defense|Mozi's Banner System for Siege Defense / 墨子旗幟制度]] — Mozi's systematic color-coded banner system for identifying defenders, materials, and military roles during siege warfare.
- [[mozi-cloud-ladder-defense-beiti|Mozi on Cloud Ladder Defense / 墨子備梯]] — A chapter from the Mozi discussing defensive strategies against cloud ladders in siege warfare, featuring a dialogue between Mozi and his disciple Qin Guli.
- [[mozi-defending-city-walls-beichengmen|Defending City Walls (Mozi) / 墨子備城門]] — A Mohist military defense treatise detailing systematic strategies for city wall protection against twelve siege methods, emphasizing preparation, material readiness, and coordinated defender response.
- [[mozi-jie-yong-upper-frugality|Mozi on Frugality (節用上) / 墨子節用上]] — A Mohist chapter advocating efficient governance through eliminating wasteful expenditures and prioritizing practical utility in clothing, shelter, arms, and transportation.
- [[mozi-ming-gui-ghost-existence-argument|Mozi's Argument for Ghost Existence / 墨子明鬼——鬼神存在之論證]] — Mozi's philosophical argument demonstrating the existence of ghosts and spirits through empirical evidence and classical texts, serving as moral governance through supernatural retribution.
- [[mozi-miscellaneous-defense-zashou|Miscellaneous Defense (雜守) / 墨子·雜守]] — A Mozi chapter detailing comprehensive urban defense strategies against siege warfare, covering tactical formations, garrison organization, supply management, and beacon communication systems.
- [[mozi-practical-standards-utilitarian-criteria|Mozi's Practical Standards for Governance / 墨子實用標準]] — Mozi's criteria for evaluating the utility of clothing, shelter, weapons, and transportation in governance decisions.
- [[mozi-preparing-against-tunnel-attacks|Preparing Against Tunnel Attacks (Mozi Chapter on Underground Defense) / 墨子備穴]] — A defensive warfare chapter from the Mozi text detailing strategies to detect and counter enemy tunneling attacks under city walls using acoustic detection, smoke熏攻, and structural defenses.
- [[mozi-qin-shi-cherishing-scholars|Mozi Chapter on Cherishing Scholars / 墨子親士]] — A chapter from the Mozi emphasizing that rulers must cherish and draw close to worthy scholars to preserve their states and achieve success.
- [[mozi-shang-xian-upper|Exalting the Virtuous (尚賢上) / 尚賢上]] — A chapter from the Mozi advocating that rulers should promote virtuous and capable individuals regardless of their social status, emphasizing that the selection of worthy ministers is the foundation of good governance.
- [[mozi-siege-commands-hao-ling|Mozi's Siege Commands and Military Orders / 墨子號令]] — This chapter from the Mozi text details the command system, military discipline, spy operations, and organizational protocols for siege defense, emphasizing strict hierarchy and reward-punishment mechanisms.
- [[mozi-siege-defense-inventory|Mozi's Siege Defense Inventory Standards / 墨子守城物資儲備法]] — Standardized material requirements for city defense including provisions, weapons, and strategic supplies in Mozi's defensive doctrine.
- [[mozi-signal-communication-siege-defense|Mozi's Signal Communication Protocol / 墨子旗鼓信號制度]] — The drum and banner signal system for siege defense communication, establishing coded responses for enemy positions and defensive responses.
- [[mozi-suo-ran-being-infected|Being Infected (所染) / 所染]] — A Mohist chapter discussing how both individuals and nations are shaped by the influences and associations they are exposed to, using the silk-dyeing analogy.
- [[mozi-three-standards-three-fa|Mozi's Three Standards / 墨子三法]] — Mozi's methodological framework of three standards for evaluating discourse: examination of ancient records, investigation of common experience, and practical application in governance.
- [[mozi-water-defense-strategies|Mozi's Water Defense Strategies / 墨子備水戰術]] — A chapter from the Mozi detailing defensive preparations and tactical responses against water attacks on fortified cities, including drainage systems, naval organization, and coordinated counterattacks.
- [[mozi-yingdi-ci-qi-observation-military-divination|Qi Observation in Military Divination / 望氣與軍事占卜]] — A Mozi passage describing techniques of observing vital energy (qi) to predict military outcomes, identifying five types of qi that reveal成败吉凶 on the battlefield.
- [[mozi-yingdi-ci-welcoming-enemy-rituals|Mozi Welcoming Enemy Rituals / 墨子迎敵祠]] — A Mozi chapter describing elaborate ritual protocols for welcoming enemy forces from the four cardinal directions, with corresponding altars, officials, colors, and military preparations.
- [[qie-ji-theft-covetous-disease|The Theory of Theft Disease (竊疾) / 竊疾論]] — Mozi's critique of the "theft disease" - a psychological condition of covetousness that afflicts both individuals and states, demonstrated through the analogy of stealing food while having plenty.
- [[qin-guli|Qin Guli / 禽滑釐]] — A devoted disciple of Mozi who served him for three years, later becoming a key figure in Mohist defensive military thought.
- [[shang-tong-reward-punishment-maf|Reward and Punishment in Shang Tong Theory / 尚同賞罰論]] — Mozi's theory of reward and punishment as the mechanism for achieving social order through unified standards of the superior.
- [[shang-xian-esteeming-worthy-part-two|Shang Xian (Esteeming the Worthy, Part 2) / 尚賢下]] — Mozi's argument that rulers must appoint the worthy and capable to governance, not favor relatives or the handsome, illustrated through historical examples of sage kings selecting ministers.
- [[shang-xian-exalting-worthy-mozi|Exalting the Worthy (尚賢) in Mozi / 墨子尚賢思想]] — Mozi's doctrine on selecting worthy and capable individuals for government positions, emphasizing merit over kinship as the foundation of good governance.
- [[shang-xian-middle-mozi|Shang Xian Zhong (Exalting the Worthy, Part 2) / 尚賢中]] — The second chapter of Mozi's Exalting the Worthy doctrine, presenting the "Three Foundations" theory and historical exemplars of sage kings who achieved governance through elevating worthy ministers.
- [[three-dukes-gong-sann-gong|Three Dukes (Sān Gōng) / 三公]] — The three highest-ranking officials in ancient Chinese imperial governance, serving as advisors to the Son of Heaven, as described in Mozi's Shang Tong.
- [[tian-xia-zhi-yi-righteousness-under-heaven|Righteousness Under Heaven / 天下之義]] — Mozi's concept of unified moral order under heaven, advocating that all people should align their standards of righteousness with those of their superiors.
- [[tu-men-tunnel-gates-city-defense|Tumen (Tunnel Gates) / 突門（城門突入口）]] — Tumen were hidden tunnel gate passages built into city walls at intervals of every hundred paces, designed as defensive traps against underground siege attacks using kilns, bellows, and smoke.
- [[yun-ti-cloud-ladder|Cloud Ladder / 雲梯]] — An ancient Chinese siege weapon, a heavy mobile tower used to scale city walls, against which Mozi developed sophisticated defensive strategies.

## Category:Other

- [[agama-explanation-twelve-links-dependent-origination|Āgama Explanation of Twelve Links of Dependent Origination / 阿含口解十二因緣經]] — A Han Dynasty Buddhist sutra on the Twelve Links of Dependent Origination, translated by An Shigao with unique inner-outer correlation teachings and karmic analysis.
- [[agricultural-foundation|Agricultural Foundation / 农本思想]] — Mencius's governance principle that agricultural development is fundamental to state prosperity
- [[an-shigao-seven-places-three-contemplations|An Shigao's Contribution: Seven Places and Three Contemplations / 安世高與七處三觀經]] — The Han dynasty translator An Shigao's systematic introduction of Buddhist meditative analysis through his translation of the Seven Places and Three Contemplations sutra.
- [[an-shigao-translated-agama-zhengxing-sutra|Fo Shuo Ahán Zhèng Xíng Jīng (The Sutra of Proper Conduct in Āgama) / 佛說阿含正行經]] — An Eastern Han translation by An Shigao presenting core Buddhist teachings on proper conduct, the five thieves, and mental cultivation.
- [[an-shigao-translation-methodology|An Shigao's Translation Methodology / 安世高譯經方法]] — The translation techniques and contribution of An Shigao, the seminal Parthian monk who translated over 90 Buddhist texts into Chinese during the Eastern Han dynasty.
- [[ananda-compiled-scriptures|阿難集經 Ānanda's Compilation of the Buddhist Canon]] — The Buddha's attendant who compiled the sutras after the Buddha's parinirvana, organizing them into the three treasures and four collections.
- [[arhat-stages-buddhist-liberation|阿羅漢位 / Stages of Arhat Liberation]] — The systematic classification of Buddhist liberation stages from stream-enterer to fully accomplished arhat, as presented in classical Indian Buddhist texts.
- [[ba-en-pin|Ba-en-pin / 报答父母恩品]] — A genre of Chinese Buddhist literature focusing on repaying parental kindness through spiritual practice.
- [[ba-yi-ceremonial-dance|Ba Yi (Eight Rows) / 八佾]] — The ceremonial dance of eight rows of eight performers, a symbol of ritual order and social hierarchy in ancient Chinese rites.
- [[bao-en-pin|報恩品 / The Chapter on Repaying Kindness (Bao'en Pin)]] — A major chapter of the Mahāyāna Sūtra on the Cultivation of the Mind-Ground, systematically explaining the Buddhist doctrine of repaying four kinds of kindness.
- [[baopuzi-chapter-14-golden-elixir-only-path|Golden Elixir as the Sole Path to Immortality / 抱朴子卷十四：金丹為不死之正道]] — Ge Hong's emphatic assertion that only the Golden Elixir (金丹) constitutes true immortality, dismissing rituals, prayers, and supernatural powers as insufficient.
- [[baopuzi-chapter-14-importance-of-seeking-master|The Importance of Seeking a True Master in Baopuzi / 抱朴子卷十四：求师问道]] — Ge Hong's discourse on the rarity of authentic Daoist masters and the necessity of sincere, diligent seeking in cultivation practice.
- [[baopuzi-chapter-14-life-brevity-calculation|Life's Brevity and Urgency in Baopuzi / 抱朴子卷十四：人生短促之歎]] — Ge Hong's vivid calculation of human lifespan, comparing life to a sacrificial animal approaching the slaughterhouse, emphasizing the urgency of cultivation practice.
- [[baopuzi-immortality-debate|Bao Puzi on Immortals / 抱朴子论神仙不死]] — Ge Hong's philosophical defense of immortality through natural transformation and historical evidence.
- [[baopuzi-jiu-dan-nine-elixirs|Nine Elixirs in Baopuzi / 抱朴子九丹]] — Baopuzi Volume 4 details the Nine Elixirs (九丹) — the supreme alchemical formulas for immortality including the Cinnabar Flower, Divine Elixir, Return Elixir, and Cold Elixir, along with the Great Clarity Elixir and Golden Liquid methods.
- [[baopuzi-selecting-daoist-texts|On Selecting Daoist Texts in Baopuzi / 抱朴子論道書之選擇]] — Ge Hong's critical assessment of various Daoist texts including the Daodejing and Zhuangzi, arguing that most are incomplete or misleading, and that true cultivation requires proper guidance rather than mere textual study.
- [[baopuzi-volume-15-grain-fasting|Grain Fasting Methods in Baopuzi / 抱朴子断穀諸法]] — Comprehensive examination of grain fasting (断穀) techniques in Ge Hong's Baopuzi, including dietary restrictions, mineral-based foods, breathing practices, and their effects on health and longevity.
- [[baopuzi-volume-17-mountain-entry|Baopuzi Volume 17: Mountain Entry Arts / 抱朴子卷十七：入山之法]] — Ge Hong's comprehensive guide to Daoist mountain entry practices, including timing, purification rituals, protective talismans, and methods for dealing with mountain spirits and dangerous creatures.
- [[baopuzi-volume-19-daoist-scriptures-catalog|Baopuzi Volume 19: Catalog of Daoist Texts / 抱朴子卷十九道書目錄]] — Ge Hong's comprehensive catalog of over 180 Daoist texts including Three Sovereigns Inner Text, Five Peaks True Form Map, talismans, alchemy scripts, and esoteric practices, as recorded from his teacher Zheng Jun.
- [[baopuzi-yellow-white-alchemy|Baopuzi on Yellow and White Alchemy / 抱朴子論黃白之術]] — Volume 16 of Ge Hong's Baopuzi presents a systematic exposition of 黄白术 (transmutation alchemy), defending its legitimacy and providing detailed alchemical formulas for creating gold and silver.
- [[bian-shi-wei-zhi|Transforming Knowledge into Wisdom / 變識為智]] — The Daoist philosophical concept of transforming rigid consciousness (識) into flexible wisdom (智), a key theme in Guanyinzi Chapter 5.
- [[bihuajing|The "Sad Flower Sutra" / 《悲華經》]] — The "Sad Flower Sutra" is a Mahayana Buddhist text encompassing teachings delivered by the Buddha on various profound subjects.
- [[bimbisara-king-magadha-ren-xian|King Bimbisara / 頻婆娑羅王]] — The Magadha king devoted to the Buddha, whose past life as a "Human Immortal" attained stream-entry, now reborn as a celestial prince.
- [[bird-nali-voice-shengjing|我所鳥的故事 / 我所鳥的故事 / 「我所」鳥の物語]] — The parable of the "Mine-Owner" bird in the Shengjing, illustrating the Buddhist teaching on non-attachment and the futility of possessiveness.
- [[bodhisattva-path|The Bodhisattva Path / 菩萨道]] — The Bodhisattva path is a central aspect of Mahayana Buddhism, focusing on the aspiration to attain enlightenment for oneself and others.
- [[bodhisattva-sacrifice-king-changshou|King Changshou's Sacrifice / 長壽王的犧牲 / 長寿王の犠牲]] — The narrative archetype of King Changshou, a bodhisattva who sacrifices his kingdom and life rather than wage war, embodying Buddhist non-retaliation ideals.
- [[bodhisattva-throw-body-feed-tiger-stupa-fasheng|The Sutra of Bodhisattva Throwing His Body to Feed the Hungry Tiger and the Stupa's Origin / 菩薩投身餧餓虎起塔因緣經]] — A Buddhist sutra describing Prince Chandana's self-sacrifice to feed seven hungry tiger cubs, the subsequent stupa's miraculous healing powers, and its translator Fasheng of Northern Liang Gaochang.
- [[brahma-fourfold-teaching|Brahma's Fourfold Teaching on Liberation / 梵天王四法]] — Mahābrahmā's teachings on the four conditions for rebirth in the Brahma realm: non-self practice, one-pointedness of mind, compassionate liberation, and abandoning defilements.
- [[bu-chu-yi-sheng-yu-chu|補處 / One Life Remaining Before Buddhahood]] — The bodhisattva stage immediately before full enlightenment, having completed all but the final traces of ignorance.
- [[cakravartin-seven-treasures-buddhist-texts|Cakravartin — The Universal Monarch with Seven Treasures / 轉輪聖王七寶]] — The Cakravartin (Wheel-turning Sacred King) is a Buddhist archetype of the ideal universal monarch possessing seven precious treasures, described extensively in the Ding Sheng Wang Karma Sutra.
- [[changahan-jing|Chang Ahan Jing (Long Discourses of the Buddha) / 長阿含經]] — The Dīrgha-āgama, the longest collection of the Buddha's long discourses in early Buddhist scripture, compiled in four sections and five recitations.
- [[changahan-shi-bao-jing|Chang A Han Shi Bao Jing (Long Discourses Tenfold Teachings Sutra) / 長阿含十報法經]] — An early Buddhist sutra presenting systematic teachings from one to ten, translated by An Shigao during the Eastern Han dynasty.
- [[chaou-ke|Chaou K'e / 赵岐]] — Han dynasty scholar who created the first major commentary on Mencius
- [[clan-lineage-system-daxizhuan|The Clan Lineage System in Daxizhuan / 禮記大傳宗法制度]] — The Daxizhuan outlines the "separate branch" (別子為祖) lineage system that governed kinship organization, ancestral worship, and inheritance in ancient Chinese society.
- [[compassionate-dragon-king-naga|Compassionate Dragon King (慈心龍王) — Buddhist Narrative of Non-Retaliation / 慈心龍王消伏怨害緣起]] — A Jataka tale depicting a dragon king who conquers the golden-winged garuda through loving-kindness and non-retaliation, exemplifying the power of compassion over violence.
- [[confucian-gender-roles-neize-education|Gender-Specific Education in the Rites / 男女之教]] — Confucian gender-differentiated education practices, with boys learning the Six Arts and girls learning women's affairs for their designated domestic and social roles.
- [[confucian-music-yue|Confucian View of Music (Yue) / 儒家的音乐观（乐）]] — Confucian philosophy on the moral and social functions of music in maintaining ritual order and personal cultivation.
- [[da-cheng-ben-sheng-xin-di-guan-jing|大乘本生心地觀經 / Mahāyāna Sūtra on the Cultivation of the Mind-Ground]] — A major Mahāyāna Buddhist sutra translated into Chinese during the Tang dynasty, teaching the cultivation of the mind-ground and repaying the four kinds of kindness.
- [[da-cheng-li-wen-zi-pu-guang-ming-zang-jing|Mahāyāna Sutra of Universal Light Treasury Transcending Words / 大乘離文字普光明藏經]] — A Mahāyāna Buddhist sutra translated by Divākara during the Tang Dynasty, teaching what bodhisattvas should abandon and realize.
- [[da-fangbian-fo-baoen-jing|Great Expedient Sutra on Repaying Buddha's Kindness / 大方便佛報恩經]] — A Mahayana sutra teaching the doctrine of repaying the Four Kindnesses through filial piety and bodhisattva practice.
- [[dacheng-bensheng-xindi-guanjing-kewen|大乘本生心地觀經淺註科文 / Commentary Outline on the Mahayana Mind-Ground Contemplation Sutra]] — A comprehensive structural outline and commentary classifying the contents of the Mahayana Sutra of Mind-Ground Contemplation into prefaces, main text, and circulation sections with detailed doctrinal divisions.
- [[dacheng-xindi-guanjing-san-shen|如來三身 / Three Bodies of the Tathagata (三身說)]] — The doctrinal classification of the Buddha's three bodies—Dharma-body, Enjoyment-body, and Transformational body—as expounded in the Mahayana Mind-Ground Contemplation Sutra, with detailed elaboration of their characteristics and salvific functions.
- [[dana-paramita-bodhisattva-giving|Dāna Pāramitā / 檀波羅蜜 / 檀波羅蜜]] — The perfection of giving in Mahayana Buddhism, exemplified by bodhisattvas who sacrifice everything for the welfare of beings.
- [[dao-de-jing-silk-manuscript|Dao De Jing (Silk Manuscript) / 道德經帛書本 / 道德経帛書本]] — The Dao De Jing Silk Manuscript presents the earliest complete version of Laozi's text, with its distinctive chapter ordering placing virtue before the Way.
- [[dayi-jing-great-meaning-sutra|Dayi Jing — The Sutra of the Great Meaning / 大意經]] — A Buddhist narrative sutra from the Song Dynasty describing the bodhisattva Dayi's vow to aid all beings, his quest for seven treasures, and his encounters with four jeweled cities before becoming a Buddha.
- [[defilement-accumulation-in-practice|Defilement Accumulation in Religious Practice / 修行中的烦恼随增]] — Buddhist teaching that external religious practices can still accumulate mental defilements when motivated by pride, desire for respect, jealousy, or other afflictions.
- [[deguang-taizi-jing-sutra|Sutra of Prince Deguang / 德光太子經]] — A Buddhist sutra recounting Prince Deguang's renunciation of royal comforts and his quest for Buddhist enlightenment, featuring teachings on the four pure practices and warnings against贪欲 and放逸.
- [[ding-fen-determining-names-positions|Determining Names and Positions (定分) / 定分]] — The Shang Yang doctrine establishing clear legal definitions of social roles and property rights as the foundation for orderly governance and the prevention of social chaos.
- [[ding-sheng-wang-king-caitanya-dhrtarastra|King Ding Sheng (Ding Sheng Wang) / 頂生王]] — King Ding Sheng is a bodhisattva incarnation who was born from his father's crown, practiced generous giving, conquered the four continents, and ascended through the thirty-three heavens, illustrating Buddhist teachings on merit and the dangers of greed.
- [[ding-sheng-wang-king-mahadyuti-origin-karma|King Ding Sheng (Mahādyuti) — Birth from the Crown and Karmic Journey / 頂生王因緣經 — 頂上化生之因緣敘事]] — A Buddhist Jataka-style narrative recounting how King Mahādyuti, born from his father's crown, conquers the four continents and ascends to Trayastriṃśa Heaven through accumulated merit.
- [[ding-sheng-wang-yinyuan-jing|The Discourse on King Śuddhodana's Previous Life / 頂生王因緣經]] — A Mahayana sutra describing the Buddha's previous incarnation as King Śuddhodana, a cakravartin who practiced extreme generosity and ruled over the four great continents and the heavenly realms.
- [[doctrine-of-the-mean|Doctrine Of The Mean]] — 
- [[eightfold-noble-path-human-immortal-sutra|Eightfold Noble Path (Human Immortal Sutra) / 八正道]] — The Eightfold Noble Path as expounded in the Sutra of the Human Immortal, taught by Mahabrahma Deva as the method for achieving pure contemplation and liberation.
- [[elderly-care-ran-yang-rites-records|Elderly Care (Yang Lao) in the Rites / 養老禮]] — Confucian rites and practices for caring for the elderly, detailing progressive support based on age, from dietary provisions to royal visits.
- [[entry-all-knowledge-dharani-gate|入一切種智行陀羅尼門 / Entry into the All-Knowledge Dhāraṇī Gate]] — A profound Mahāyāna dhāraṇī practice for entering complete wisdom, enabling practitioners to obtain countless samādhis,Store dhāraṇīs, and achieve supreme enlightenment.
- [[erya-classic-chinese-glossary|Erya (Classic of Correct Rhymes) / 爾雅]] — The Erya is China's oldest comprehensive glossary, compiled during the Warring States-Han period, providing definitions of classical terms across categories with phonetic annotations.
- [[evil-classification-buddhism-e|Evil and Unwholesome Qualities / 惡 / 悪]] — Buddhist classification of unwholesome qualities including bodily, verbal, and mental misconduct, arising from the three poisons.
- [[evil-section-three-dharmas-sanfang-dunlun|Evil Section (惡品) in the Three Dharmas Treatise / 三法度論惡品]] — The second chapter of the Three Dharmas Treatise examining evil deeds, desire, and delusion as the three unwholesome roots.
- [[fa-ju-monk|Fajü (法炬) — Western Jin Buddhist Translator / 法炬]] — Fajü was a Buddhist monk from the Western Jin dynasty who translated multiple sutras including the Sutra of the Three Cycles of Past Lives.
- [[fenbie-gongde-lun|分別功德論 (Fenbie Gongde Lun / Analysis of Merits Treatise)]] — A Buddhist treatise explaining the merits of arhats, the Buddha's disciples, and the compilation of the Three Treasuries.
- [[first-principle-shangjun-shu|First Principle (壹言) / 壹言]] — A foundational concept from the Book of Lord Shang emphasizing the unity of state power and the importance of concentrating national effort on agriculture and military affairs.
- [[five-aggregates-contemplation-buddhist|Five Aggregates Contemplation / 五陰觀 / 五蘊の観想]] — Systematic contemplation on the five aggregates (form, sensation, perception, formations, consciousness) as a path to understanding non-self and achieving liberation.
- [[five-aggregates-seven-aspects-an-shigao|Five Aggregates Analyzed Through Seven Aspects / 五蘊七事分析法]] — An Shigao's systematic method of analyzing each of the five aggregates (form, feeling, perception, formations, consciousness) through seven contemplative aspects.
- [[five-ascetics-seven-śrāvaka-buddhist-narrative|五仙人的故事與七覺支的象徵意義 / 五仙人故事與七覺支象徵意義 / 五仙人の物語と七覚支の象徴的意義]] — The narrative of the five ascetics in the Shengjing, illustrating Buddhist teachings on karma, rebirth, and the development of the seven factors of awakening.
- [[five-bliss-food-offering-sutra|Sutra on Five Blessings from Food Offerings / 佛說食施獲五福報經]] — A Buddhist sutra teaching that providing food to others generates five types of blessings: life, complexion, strength, peace, and eloquence.
- [[five-categories-people-wumin-shangjunshu|Five Categories of People / 五民]] — The Five Categories (五民) refers to Lord Shang's classification of social groups—scholars, hermits, warriors, artisans, and merchants—with their respective roles and governance implications.
- [[five-hindrances-ten-fetters-buddhist-doctrine|Five Hindrances and Ten Fetters in Buddhist Doctrine / 五葢十纏]] — A comprehensive explanation of the five hindrances (五葢) that obscure the mind and ten fetters (十纏) that bind beings to samsara, from the Mahāyāna Mind-Ground Sutra commentary.
- [[five-peaks-true-form-map-wuyue-zhenxing-tu|Five Peaks True Form Map / 五嶽真形圖]] — A most sacred Taoist talisman text described in Baopuzi as requiring blood oaths, forty-year transmission cycles, and possessing powers to ward off evil, heal diseases, cross waters, and reveal hidden knowledge.
- [[five-roots-five-powers-an-shigao-commentary|Five Roots and Five Powers / 五根五力]] — The Five Roots (信進念定慧) and Five Powers (信力精進力念力定力慧力) as expounded in An Shigao's Han Dynasty Buddhist commentary.
- [[five-thieves-buddhist-doctrine|Five Thieves / 五賊]] — Buddhist doctrine of the five mental thieves that lead beings to evil rebirth
- [[five-virtues-four-vices|Five Virtues and Four Vices / 五美四恶]] — Confucius's political philosophy outlining five virtues to cultivate and four vices to avoid in governance
- [[fixed-livelihood|Fixed Livelihood / 恒产论]] — Mencius's economic theory that stable property ownership is essential for moral stability
- [[foshuo-pusa-benxing-jing|Bodhisattva Practice Sutra / 佛說菩薩本行經]] — A Buddhist sutra (3 volumes) depicting Jataka tales of past Buddha lives, emphasizing the bodhisattva path through charity, sacrifice, and perseverance.
- [[four-agamas-commentary-commentary-on-four-collections|Four Āgamas Commentary / 四阿鋡暮抄解]] — A Buddhist philosophical commentary on the Four Āgamas discussing the Three Dharmas of merit, evil, and liberation.
- [[four-agnas-four-absorptions-buddhist-meditation|四種阿那般那 / Four Ānāpānas / 四つの阿那般那]] — A Buddhist meditation practice involving four types of breath contemplation and mental development stages.

- [[four-inversions-buddhist|Four Inversions / 四顛倒 / 四颠倒]] — The four inverted or perverted views that afflict sentient beings, mistaking suffering as happiness, impermanence as permanence, non-self as self, and impurity as purity.

- [[shang-tong-identifying-with-superiors|shang-tong-identifying-with-superiors]] — The article explores Mozi's arguments for hierarchical uniformity, emphasizing how a well-structured governance system with unified moral standards and a clear reward-punishment mechanism—spanning from the Son of Heaven down to village leaders—is essential for maintaining order and preventing chaos.
- [[shang-tong-upward-conformity|shang-tong-upward-conformity]] — This article explains Mozi's argument that social order requires rulers to understand the people's true sentiments and establish unified standards of righteousness through a hierarchical governance system, preventing the chaos that naturally arises when each person follows their own individual standards.
- [[shang-tong-upward-uniformity-mozi|shang-tong-upward-uniformity-mozi]] — This article explains Mozi's "Shang Tong Xia" doctrine, which establishes a four-tier hierarchical political system where unity and moral alignment flow downward from family to state to world to heaven, with the key principle that rulers must understand the true situation of their people to properly govern through rewards and punishments.
- [[sheng-jing-birth-sutras|Sheng Jing (Birth Sutras) / 生經]] — A Buddhist sutra collection translated by Zhu Fahu during the Western Jin dynasty, containing ten narratives illustrating karmic principles and monastic discipline.

- [[shi-men-tong-pan|十門通判 / Ten-Fold Framework for Sutra Exposition]] — A systematic ten-category methodology for analyzing and expounding Buddhist sutras, originating with Xianshou Fazang and elaborated by later masters.
