- [[shizi-yue-fo-ben-sheng-jing|The Lion-Moon Buddha Jataka Sutra / 師子月佛本生經]] — A Buddhist Jataka sutra describing how a monkey who received the Five Precepts from an arhat was reborn over multiple lives and eventually became the Buddha Shi Zi Yue (Lion-Moon), with 84,000 golden monkeys receiving bodhisattva predictions.
- [[shou-yi-zhi-dao-guarding-the-one|Guarding the One (守一之道) / 守一之道]] — A fundamental Daoist practice of maintaining singular focus on the Dao for immortality, protection, and spiritual transformation, as described in Baopuzi.
- [[si-en-four-graces-buddhism|Four Graces / 四恩 / 四恩]] — Buddhist doctrine of repaying four kinds of kindness: parents, sentient beings, ruler, and Triple Gem
- [[si-en|四恩 / Four Kindnesses / 四恩（しおりん）]] — The Buddhist teaching on four debts of gratitude—to parents, teachers, sovereign, and sentient beings—that form the foundation of Buddhist ethical practice.
- [[si-yuan-four-vows-bodhisattva-practice-yue-ming-jing|Four Vows (四願) in the Moonlight Bodhisattva Sutra / 月明童子經四願——菩薩修行之根本誓願]] — The Four Vows are the fundamental commitments bodhisattvas make for spiritual practice, encompassing skillful means, spiritual friendship, giving, and dharma practice.
- [[sima-fa-methods-of-the-marshal|Methods of the Marshal / 司馬法]] — A classical Chinese military treatise from the Warring States period, emphasizing benevolent warfare, ritual propriety in military affairs, and the integration of Confucian ethics with military strategy.
- [[six-mourning-principles-daxizhuan|The Six Principles of Mourning in Daxizhuan / 禮記大傳服術六法]] — The Daxizhuan enumerates six principles (服術) governing mourning garments and kinship obligations: 親親, 尊尊, 名, 出入, 長幼, 從服.
- [[sumati-woman-buddhist-narrative|Sumati (Xumoti) — Buddhist Laywoman Narrative / 須摩提女——佛教在家女性敘事]] — The story of Sumati, a Buddhist laywoman whose past-life vow during Kashapa Buddha's time leads to mass conversion and spiritual liberation in the present.
- [[sun-tzu-art-of-war|Sun Tzu's Art of War / 孫子兵法 / 孫氏兵法]] — An ancient Chinese military treatise by Sun Tzu consisting of thirteen chapters covering strategic principles, tactics, intelligence gathering, and the philosophy of warfare.
- [[tai-shang-gan-ying-pian|Tai Shang Gan Ying Pian / 太上感應篇]] — A foundational Daoist moral treatise on karmic retribution, emphasizing that fortune and misfortune are not arbitrary but arise from one's own actions.
- [[tai-xi-embryo-breathing-baopuzi|Embryo Breathing (胎息) in Baopuzi / 抱朴子中的胎息之法]] — A detailed examination of the embryo breathing technique (胎息) described in Baopuzi as the supreme method of qi cultivation, enabling practitioners to breathe without using nose or mouth as if in the womb.
- [[tathagata-eight-rare-qualities|Eight Rare Qualities of a Tathagata / 如來八希有法]] — Eight exceptional qualities that appear when a Buddha enters the world, as taught by Indra and repeated by Brahma, forming a unique doctrinal teaching of this sutra.
- [[ten-remembrances-buddhist-meditation|Ten Remembrances / 十念]] — A Buddhist meditation practice involving ten objects of mindfulness, from the Commentary on Classifying Merit.
- [[thirty-seven-bodhiparamitas-an-shigao-commentary|Thirty-Seven Bodhiparamitas / 三十七品道品 / 三十七波羅蜜]] — A detailed analysis of the thirty-seven practices leading to enlightenment as expounded in An Shigao's commentary on the Yin Chi Ru Jing.
- [[thirty-seven-bodhiparamitas-an-shigao|Thirty-Seven Factors of Enlightenment / 三十七道品]] — A systematic classification of Buddhist practice teachings organized in progressive numerical categories (1-10), as presented in An Shigao's translation of the Long Discourses.
- [[thirty-three-heavens|Trayastriṃśa Heaven / 三十三天（忉利天）]] — The Heaven of Thirty-Three Gods where the initial discourse of the Great Firm Brāhmaṇa Sūtra takes place, presided over by Śakra (帝釋天主) and the site of the first teaching of the eight rare qualities.
- [[thousand-lamp-body-offering-bodhisattva-practice|The King Who Lit a Thousand Lamps / 以身燃千燈之王]] — The Buddhist narrative of a king who sacrificed his own flesh to light a thousand lamps as the ultimate act of dedication to the Dharma.
- [[three-dharmas-buddhist-philosophy|Three Dharmas / 三法]] — A fundamental Buddhist philosophical framework comprising merit, evil, and liberation through dependent awakening.
- [[three-dharmas-framework-buddhism|Three Dharmas / 三法 / 三法]] — A Buddhist doctrinal framework classifying all phenomena into three categories: virtue (德), evil (惡), and basis (依), each containing three subcategories.
- [[three-evil-roots-buddhist|Three Evil Roots / 三惡本 / 三悪根本]] — The three fundamental sources of unwholesome karma: greed (贪), hatred (恚), and delusion (痴), from which all other evils arise.
- [[three-poisons-greed-hatred-delusion-buddhist-teaching|三毒的業報與解脫之道 / 三毒的業報與解脫之道 / 三毒の業報と解脱への道]] — Buddhist teachings on the three poisons (贪瞋痴) and their role in binding beings to samsara, as illustrated through multiple narratives in the Shengjing.
- [[three-roots-of-unwholesomeness|Three Roots of Unwholesomeness / 三不善根]] — The three fundamental unwholesome mental roots—greed, hatred, and delusion—that underlie all negative karmic actions in Buddhism.
- [[three-treasures|Three Treasures / 三宝]] — The three foundational refuges of Buddhism—Buddha, Dharma, and Sangha—considered precious objects of veneration and sources of spiritual refuge.
- [[three-treasuries-four-collections|三藏三分 Four Āgamas / Tripartite Canon and Quadruple Sūtra Collections]] — The organization of the Buddhist canon into three treasures and four sūtra collections, attributed to Ānanda's compilation guided by celestial beings.
- [[three-types-liberation-buddhist-uppsala|Three Types of Liberation in Buddhist Practice / 佛教三種解脫]] — The classification of liberation into desire liberation, form liberation, and cessation absorption, as discussed in the Three Dharmas Treatise.
- [[three-unifications-legalism-yi-shang-yi-xing-yi-jiao|Three Unifications in Legalism / 壹賞壹刑壹教]] — Lord Shang's doctrine of unified rewards, unified punishment, and unified teaching as the three pillars of Legalist state governance.
- [[three-vermin-three-shixing-shangjunshu|Three Vermin / 三蝨]] — The Three Vermin (三蝨) concept from the Book of Lord Shang describes three parasitic forces that weaken a state: poverty, wealth, and moral corruption.
- [[throw-body-feed-tigers-jataka|Throw Body to Feed Tigers (投身飼虎) - Jataka Tale of Prince Mahāsattva]] — The Jataka story of Prince Mahāsattva who sacrificed his body to feed seven starving tiger cubs, a paradigm of ultimate bodhisattva compassion.
- [[toutuo-xing|頭陀行 / Dhutanga Practices]] — 頭陀行乃佛教十三種清淨苦行，修習此法可去衣、食、住之貪著，速得解脫
- [[turtle-monkey-past-life-karmic-narrative-shengjing|鱉獼猴前世的業報故事 / 鱉と獼猴の前世因果物語 / 거북이와 원숭이의 전생 업보 이야기]] — The turtle and monkey past-life karmic connection in the Shengjing, illustrating how past-life relationships manifest in the present and the consequences of broken trust.
- [[twelve-links-dependent-origination-an-shigao-commentary|Twelve Links of Dependent Origination / 十二因緣 / 十二縁起]] — Analysis of the twelve links of dependent origination as explained in An Shigao's commentary on the Yin Chi Ru Jing.
- [[twelve-links-dependent-origination|Twelve Links of Dependent Origination / 十二因緣]] — The Buddhist doctrine explaining the cyclical chain of causation from ignorance to suffering.
- [[upaya-expedient-means-buddhism|Expedient Means / 方便 / 方便]] — Buddhist concept of upaya (expedient means) as the practical methods and path structures for achieving spiritual liberation.
- [[upaya-skillful-means-three-dharmas|Skillful Means (方便) in the Three Dharmas Treatise / 三法度論方便]] — The concept of skillful means (upāya) as the path leading to liberation, comprising precepts, concentration, and wisdom.
- [[virama-bodhisattva-pusajiamo|Vīrāma (毘羅摩) — Bodhisattva of Giving]] — A minister's son who became chief minister and exemplified the perfection of giving through vast generosity and skillful means.
- [[virtue-merit-buddhism-de|Merit and Virtue in Buddhist Practice / 德 / 徳]] — Buddhist concept of merit (德, puṇya) encompassing giving, morality, meditation, and the three roots of wholesome qualities.
- [[virtue-merit-buddhist-doctrine-de-pin|Virtue Section (德品) - Buddhist Spiritual Cultivation]] — The first section of the Three Dharmas Treatise detailing the cultivation of merit, roots of goodness, and non-evil qualities.
- [[void-seal-bodhisattva|虛空印菩薩 / Void Seal Bodhisattva (Xūkōng Yìn Púsà)]] — A bodhisattva in Mahāyāna Buddhism who received the teaching of all-knowledge dhāraṇī and later became the Lotus-Up Tathāgata in the Lotus World.
- [[wen-sang-mourning-staff-ji|The Mourning Staff in the Book of Rites / 問喪中的喪杖制度]] — A Confucian analysis of mourning ritual implements, particularly the mourning staff (杖) made from different materials for father and mother mourning, and the mourning cap (免).
- [[white-cloth-golden-banner-two-brahmins-origin-sutra|White Cloth and Golden Banner Two Brahmins Origin Sutra / 白衣金幢二婆羅門緣起經]] — A Buddhist sutra recounting the renunciation of two Brahmins and presenting a Buddhist cosmology of human social origins.
- [[wu-pu-five-animal-play-hua-tuo|Wu Pu and the Five Animal Play / 吴普与五禽戏]] — Wu Pu, student of physician Hua Tuo, practiced the Five Animal Play (Wu Qin Xi) and achieved longevity over 100 years, demonstrating the health benefits of Daoist physical cultivation.
- [[wu-zhi-five-fungi-baopuzi|Five Fungi (五芝) in Baopuzi / 抱朴子五芝]] — The classification and effects of five types of fungi (石芝、木芝、草芝、肉芝、菌芝) for immortality in Daoist alchemy.
- [[wu-zi|Wu Zi / 吳子]] — A classical Chinese military treatise by Wu Qi, presenting principles of state governance, military strategy, troop discipline, and leadership through dialogues with King Wu of Wei.
- [[xianshou-wu-jiao|賢首五教 / Five Teachings of Xianshou / 賢首五教（けんじゅぎょう）]] — A five-tiered doctrinal classification system developed by Fazang (Xianshou) of the Huayan school, categorizing all Buddhist teachings from Hinayana to the highest Yogacara-Tathagatagarbha doctrines.
- [[xu-fen-buddhist-prologue|序分 / Buddhist Prologue Section]] — The introductory section of Buddhist sutras establishing credibility and context for the main teachings.
- [[yi-wei-shi-wo-yi-yi-wei-xin-yi|Intention as Dust, Mind as Transitory / 意者塵往來爾]] — The philosophical concept from Guanyinzi that intention (意) is merely the comings and goings of dust, while the mind (心) remains fundamentally unchanged.
- [[you-ai-gu-sheng-you-you-yin-ai-gu-sheng-kong|From Love Arises Sorrow; From Love Arises Fear / 由愛故生憂 由愛故生怖]] — A canonical Buddhist gatha stating that attachment is the origin of suffering and fear, and liberation comes from detachment.
- [[yu-ye-nu-jing-sutra|Yu Ye Nü Jing (Sutra of Lady Yu Ye) / 佛說玉耶女經]] — A Buddhist sutra teaching conjugal conduct to Lady Yu Ye, featuring the famous doctrine of Seven Types of Wives.
- [[yue-ming-tongzi-moonlight-youth-bodhisattva-sutra|Moonlight Youth (月明童子) — Protagonist of the Moonlight Bodhisattva Sutra / 月明童子——《月光菩薩經》的主人公]] — The Moonlight Youth (月明童子) is a clean-minded young man addressed by the Buddha, symbolizing purity of mind in the sutra.
- [[yue-shang-rulai-moon-topped-tathagata|Moon-Topped Tathāgata / 月上如來]] — Moon-Topped Tathāgata (月上如來) is a historical Buddha described in the Mahāyāna Dhāraṇī of Compassion, predecessor of the Lotus-Up Tathāgata.
- [[zhang-liang-daoist-cultivation-exile|Zhang Liang's Daoist Cultivation and Exile / 张良修道绝谷]] — Zhang Liang (Zhang Liang), famous strategist of the Han founding, abandoned worldly affairs to pursue Daoist cultivation and practices of fasting (绝谷), demonstrating historical evidence for immortality cultivation.
- [[zigong|Zigong / 子贡]] — A prominent disciple of Confucius known for diplomatic skill and commercial success.
- [[さとり|Satori / 悟]] — Satori is a Japanese Buddhist term for a sudden awakening or enlightenment experience, often associated with Zen practice.
- [[七覺意注-(安世高)|Seven Factors of Enlightenment Commentary (An Shigao) / 七覺意注（安世高）]] — An early Chinese commentary by An Shigao on the seven factors of enlightenment within the thirty‑seven bodhiparamitas.
- [[五根五力注-(安世高)|Five Roots and Five Powers Commentary (An Shigao) / 五根五力注 (安世高)]] — Commentary on the Five Roots and Five Powers by the early Chinese Buddhist translator An Shigao, forming part of the systematic exposition of the thirty‑seven bodhipāramitās.
- [[如来八寶塔-eight-tathagata-stupas|Eight Tathāgata Stupas / 如來八寶塔 / 如来八宝塔]] — The eight sacred stupas representing key events in the Buddha's life, described in the Mahāyāna Mind-Ground Contemplation Sūtra
- [[心地法門|Mind-Ground Dharma Gate / 心地法門]] — A central Buddhist practice of cultivating and contemplating the mind-ground as the basis of spiritual awakening.

## Category:Political-Philosophy

- [[born-in-adversity-die-in-comfort|Born in Adversity, Die in Comfort / 生于忧患，死于安乐]] — Mencius' famous philosophical statement on how hardship builds character and virtue, while comfort leads to moral decline.
- [[mozi-heaven-rewards-virtue-emperor-punishment|Heaven's Rewards for Virtue and Punishment for Vice / 天賞善罰暴]] — Mozi's doctrine that Heaven rewards virtuous rulers and punishes evil ones, as illustrated through the outcomes of sage kings versus tyrants.
- [[preventing-speech-damming-rivers|Preventing People's Speech is Harder than Damming Rivers / 防民之口甚於防川]] — Duke Shao's famous political metaphor warning that suppressing criticism is more dangerous than damming rivers.

## Category:Self-Cultivation

- [[extending-kindness-pushing-grace-tui-en|Extending Kindness (推恩) / 推恩]] — Mencius's doctrine that one should extend one's natural care from self and family to all people.
- [[guarding-emptiness-void-wenzi-xu|Guarding Emptiness (守虛) in Wenzi / 文子"守虛"論]] — Guarding Emptiness (守虛) is the foundational Daoist practice in Wenzi Volume 3, emphasizing the cultivation of inner emptiness and receptivity as the gateway to understanding the Dao and achieving spiritual clarity.
- [[knowing-destiny-rites-words|Knowing Destiny, Rites, and Words / 知命知礼知言]] — Confucius's three essential knowledges for becoming a true gentleman in the Analects
- [[li-ji-guan-yi-meaning-capping-rite|The Meaning of the Capping Rite / 禮記·冠義]] — A classical Confucian text from the Book of Rites explaining the ritual significance of the capping ceremony as the foundation of all ritual propriety and the gateway to adult moral responsibility.
- [[mengzi-haoran-qi-vast-flowing-vital-energy|Vast Flowing Qi (浩然之氣) / 浩然之氣]] — Mencius's concept of moral cultivated vital energy that fills the universe when properly nurtured through accumulated righteousness.
- [[mengzi-indomitable-heart-budongxin|Indefatigable Heart (不動心) / 不動心]] — Mencius's concept of the steadfast moral heart, cultivated through courage, righteosness, and the accumulation of moral energy.

## Category:Zhuangzi

- [[de-yi-wang-yan-zhuangzi|Forget the Words When the Meaning is Understood / 得意忘言]] — Zhuangzi's philosophical principle that true understanding transcends language, illustrated through the fish trap and rabbit snare metaphors.
- [[hu-zi-huzi-zhuangzi|Huzi (壺子) - The Master of Hidden Virtue / 壺子]] — The Daoist master Huzi who demonstrated four different spiritual manifestations to the fortune-teller Jixian, illustrating the illusory nature of external judgments and the depth of inner cultivation.
- [[hubin-wheelmaking-discourse-zhuangzi|Wheelwright's Wheel-Making Discourse / 輪扁斲輪]] — A philosophical discourse in Zhuangzi where a wheelwright explains to Duke Huan why the words of the sages are merely "dregs" and true wisdom cannot be transmitted through language.
- [[liezi-journey-early-return|Liezi's Journey and Early Return / 列禦寇之齊與伯昏瞀人的故事]] — The story of Liezi journeying to Qi but turning back after becoming "startled" by receiving special treatment, illustrating the danger of being sought after by people.
- [[nanbo-ziqi-form-dead-wood-heart-dead-ashes|Nanbo Ziqi / 南伯子綦]] — A legendary Daoist sage from Zhuangzi described as sitting in meditation with "form like withered bones and heart like dead ashes," symbolizing profound spiritual realization.
- [[perfect-person-zhiren-zhuangzi|Perfect Person (Zhiren) / 至人]] — The highest ideal in Daoist cultivation - one who attains utmost beauty and joy by wandering freely beyond all transformations and attachments.
- [[remove-harmful-horses-governance|Remove the Harmful Horses / 去其害馬]] — A governance principle from Zhuangzi where the Yellow Emperor learns from a child that ruling the world is like tending horses—simply remove what harms them.
- [[shen-gui-dream-yuan-jun-zhuangzi|The Divine Turtle Story / 神龜能見夢於元君]] — The parable of the divine turtle that could appear in dreams but could not avoid the net, illustrating the limits of wisdom and foreknowledge.
- [[sun-shuao-equanimity-zhuangzi|Sun Shu'ao's Equanimity / 孫叔敖之無憂]] — The story of Sun Shu'ao who served three times as prime minister without joy and left three times without sorrow, embodying Daoist detachment from official rank.
- [[traveling-mind-origin-things-zhuangzi|Traveling Mind to the Origin of Things / 遊心於物之初]] — Laozi's teaching in Zhuangzi on the mind wandering to the primordial origin of all things, describing the state of ultimate beauty and joy.
- [[zhuangzi-fisherman-yu-fu|The Fisherman Chapter (Yu Fu) / 莊子·漁父]] — A Zhuangzi chapter featuring a Daoist fisherman who teaches Confucius about authenticity (真), criticizing artificial ritual and social conventions while advocating naturalness and genuine sincerity.
- [[zhuangzi-great-skill-appears-clumsy-da-qiao-ruo-zhuo|"Great Skill Appears Clumsy" / 大巧若拙]] — A famous Zhuangzi paradox stating that true mastery looks awkward or clumsy, while apparent skill invites theft and competition.
- [[zhuangzi-thieving-box-qu-qie|Zhuangzi's "Thieving the Box" / 莊子·胠篋]] — A Zhuangzi chapter arguing that preventive measures against petty theft enable great thieves, and that sage teachings are exploited by those who steal states.
- [[zhuangzi-zhi-bei-you-chapter|Zhi Bei You (Northern Journey of Knowledge) / 知北遊]] — Chapter 22 of Zhuangzi exploring the nature of knowledge and the omnipresence of the Dao through dialogues between Zhi, Wu Wei Wei, Kuang Qu, and Huang Di.
- [[子貢|Zigong / 子貢]] — A prominent disciple of Confucius known for diplomatic skill and commercial acumen.

## Causality

- [[fuli-prince-fortune-power-cause-effect-sutra|Fuli Prince Sutra on Merit and Fortune / 福力太子因緣經]] — A Mahayana sutra teaching that cultivating merit and fortune surpasses all other virtues, featuring Prince Fuli's story of ascent to Cakravartin kingship through supreme generosity.

## Causes-Of-Death

- [[nine-unnatural-deaths-buddhist|Nine Unnatural/Unexplained Deaths / 九橫 / 九横]] — Nine categories of untimely deaths caused by preventable causes such as improper eating, wrong conduct, and association with evil companions.

## Celestial

- [[constellation-fate-determinism-bao-puzi|Constellation-Based Fate Determinism in Bao Puzi / 抱朴子星宿命定論]] — Bao Puzi's argument that human lifespan and potential for immortality are determined by the constellation present at the time of conception, not by divine will.

## Celestial-Assembly

- [[brahma-fourfold-teaching|Brahma's Fourfold Teaching on Liberation / 梵天王四法]] — Mahābrahmā's teachings on the four conditions for rebirth in the Brahma realm: non-self practice, one-pointedness of mind, compassionate liberation, and abandoning defilements.

## Celestial-Beings

- [[human-immortal-ren-xian|Human Immortal / 人仙]] — A celestial being who is the son of Vaisravana (毘沙門天王) and serves as a messenger revealing the karmic fate of King Bimbisara.

## Celestials

- [[great-brahma-king|Great Brahma King / 大梵天王]] — A celestial deity in Buddhist cosmology who taught the Four Bases of Supernatural Power at the Thirty-three Heavens.

## Ceremony

- [[ba-yi-ceremonial-dance|Ba Yi (Eight Rows) / 八佾]] — The ceremonial dance of eight rows of eight performers, a symbol of ritual order and social hierarchy in ancient Chinese rites.
- [[liji-dahen-great-wedding-ritual|The Great Wedding Ritual (Da Hen) / 大昏——婚禮之道]] — Confucius's philosophy on the grand wedding ceremony (大昏) as the supreme form of reverence and the foundation of familial and political order.

## Cessation

- [[nirodha-samapatti|滅盡定 Nirodhāsamāpatti / Absorption of Cessation]] — A Buddhist meditation attainment where all mental formations cease, enabling practitioners to grant present-world blessings to beings.

## Change

- [[laochengzi-illusion-transformation-liezi|Lao Chengzi's Study of Illusion / 老成子學幻 / 老成子の幻化学]] — The philosophical narrative of Lao Chengzi learning the art of transformation and illusion from Yin Wen, including the Daoist theory of change and the nature of reality.

## Chaos

- [[hun-tun-chaos-death-zhuangzi|The Death of Hun-tun (渾沌之死) / 渾沌之死]] — The parable in Zhuangzi where well-intentioned intervention by 儵 and 忽 destroys the natural simplicity of 渾沌, illustrating the dangers of artificial interference with natural states.

## Chapter-22

- [[zhuangzi-zhi-bei-you-chapter|Zhi Bei You (Northern Journey of Knowledge) / 知北遊]] — Chapter 22 of Zhuangzi exploring the nature of knowledge and the omnipresence of the Dao through dialogues between Zhi, Wu Wei Wei, Kuang Qu, and Huang Di.

## Chapter-6

- [[guanyinzi-chapter-six-self-transformation|Guanyinzi Chapter Six: On the Self / 關尹子第六章：論自我]] — Chapter 6 of Guanyinzi explores the nature of self, dream versus waking states, form transformation, and the concept of no-self (無我) in Daoist philosophy.

## Chapter-9

- [[guan-yinzi-chapter-nine-medicinal-treatment|Guanyinzi Chapter Nine: Medicinal Treatment / 關尹子第九篇：藥]] — Chapter 9 of Guanyinzi presents teachings on miscellaneous remedies for spiritual and moral ailments, addressing the proper balance between wisdom, speech, and action through paradoxes and practical metaphors.
- [[guanyinzi-chapter-nine|Guanyinzi Chapter Nine: On Medicine / 關尹子第九章：藥者雜治]] — Chapter 9 of Guanyinzi presents the "medicine" metaphor for spiritual practice, discussing how the sage applies various remedies to correct imbalances between extremes.

## Character

- [[junzi|The Role of the Junzi / 君子的角色]] — Examines the characteristics and responsibilities of the Junzi in Confucian philosophy.

## Cheng

- [[shangqiu-kai-faith-moves-heaven-earth-liezi|Shangqiu Kai: Faith That Moves Heaven and Earth / 商丘開：至信感人]] — The story of Shangqiu Kai demonstrates how supreme sincerity (至信) can move heaven and earth, allowing one to walk through fire without harm.

## China

- [[han-dynasty|Han Dynasty / 汉朝]] — The Han dynasty (202 BC – 220 AD) was the second imperial dynasty of China, marking a golden age of political stability, economic prosperity, and cultural achievement.
- [[ruo-min-weakening-the-people|Weakening the People (弱民) / 弱民]] — A Legalist political doctrine advocating that rulers should deliberately weaken the populace to strengthen state power, creating dependence through poverty and labor.

## Chinese Philosophy

- [[confucian-ethics|Confucian Ethics / 儒家伦理]] — This article explores the key concepts of Confucian ethics as presented in the Analects, focusing on filial piety and social conduct.
- [[confucian-self-cultivation|Confucian Self-Cultivation / 儒家自我修养]] — The systematic practice of moral and spiritual development based on Confucian teachings.
- [[human-nature-is-good|human-nature-is-good]] — Mencius argues that human nature is inherently good, using the sincere grief during mourning rituals as evidence that moral cultivation through education can develop this innate goodness.
- [[mengzi|Mencius / 孟子]] — Mencius (c. 372–289 BCE) was the most prominent Confucian philosopher after Confucius, known for his doctrine of the innate goodness of human nature.
- [[mozi-fayi-standard-law|Mozi's Standard of Law (法儀) / 墨子法儀]] — Mozi argues that all governance requires a standard or model, and that Heaven (天) rather than parents, teachers, or rulers should serve as the ultimate ethical benchmark.
- [[mozi-jie-zang-frugal-burial|Mozi on Frugal Burial (節葬) / 墨子節葬]] — Mozi's critique of excessive burial practices and prolonged mourning, arguing for simple burials based on the examples of ancient sage kings.
- [[孟子の政治哲学|Mencius's Political Philosophy / 孟子的政治哲学]] — ... (one line)
- [[關尹子|關尹子 / Guanyinzi]] — A Daoist text attributed to Yin Xi, presenting teachings on sage governance and cosmic transformation

## Chinese-Alchemy

- [[baopuzi-volume-17-mountain-entry|Baopuzi Volume 17: Mountain Entry Arts / 抱朴子卷十七：入山之法]] — Ge Hong's comprehensive guide to Daoist mountain entry practices, including timing, purification rituals, protective talismans, and methods for dealing with mountain spirits and dangerous creatures.

## Chinese-Ancient-Philosophy

- [[mozi-gong-meng-dialogue|The Mozi-Gong Meng Dialogue / 墨子與公孟子之辯]] — A philosophical debate between Mozi and the Confucian scholar Gong Meng covering governance, ritual, fate, ghosts, and the four harmful doctrines of Confucianism.

## Chinese-Beliefs

- [[confucius-analects|Analects of Confucius / 论语]] — A collection of sayings and ideas attributed to the Chinese philosopher Confucius.

## Chinese-Buddhism

- [[agama-explanation-twelve-links-dependent-origination|Āgama Explanation of Twelve Links of Dependent Origination / 阿含口解十二因緣經]] — A Han Dynasty Buddhist sutra on the Twelve Links of Dependent Origination, translated by An Shigao with unique inner-outer correlation teachings and karmic analysis.
- [[ba-en-pin|Ba-en-pin / 报答父母恩品]] — A genre of Chinese Buddhist literature focusing on repaying parental kindness through spiritual practice.
- [[changahan-jing|Chang Ahan Jing (Long Discourses of the Buddha) / 長阿含經]] — The Dīrgha-āgama, the longest collection of the Buddha's long discourses in early Buddhist scripture, compiled in four sections and five recitations.
- [[da-cheng-ben-sheng-xin-di-guan-jing|大乘本生心地觀經 / Mahāyāna Sūtra on the Cultivation of the Mind-Ground]] — A major Mahāyāna Buddhist sutra translated into Chinese during the Tang dynasty, teaching the cultivation of the mind-ground and repaying the four kinds of kindness.
- [[fa-ju-monk|Fajü (法炬) — Western Jin Buddhist Translator / 法炬]] — Fajü was a Buddhist monk from the Western Jin dynasty who translated multiple sutras including the Sutra of the Three Cycles of Past Lives.
- [[foshuo-pusa-benxing-jing|Bodhisattva Practice Sutra / 佛說菩薩本行經]] — A Buddhist sutra (3 volumes) depicting Jataka tales of past Buddha lives, emphasizing the bodhisattva path through charity, sacrifice, and perseverance.
- [[kumarrow-translation-commentary|Kumārajīva's Translation Methodology in Four Āgamas Commentary / 鳩摩羅什譯經方法]] — Documentation of Kumārajīva's translation practices during the Former Qin dynasty, including team translation methods and philological approaches.
- [[lai-zhou-monk-commentary-dacheng-bensheng-xindi-guanjing|Lai Zhou (來舟) / 來舟法師]] — A Qing Dynasty monk who authored a major commentary on the Mahayana Mind-Ground Contemplation Sutra, synthesizing Huayan and Tiantai classification systems.
- [[liang-she-fa-two-grabbing-methods|Two Grabbing Methods / 二攝法 / 二攝法]] — The Buddhist methodology combining material giving (財法) with Dharma teaching (法施) to benefit sentient beings through both physical and spiritual means.
- [[mahayana-dharani-of-compassion|大乘悲分陀利經 / Mahāyāna Dhāraṇī of Compassion]] — A Mahāyāna sutra describing the Lotus World, the Lotus-Up Tathāgata, and the profound dhāraṇī practices for achieving supreme enlightenment.
- [[shi-men-tong-pan|十門通判 / Ten-Fold Framework for Sutra Exposition]] — A systematic ten-category methodology for analyzing and expounding Buddhist sutras, originating with Xianshou Fazang and elaborated by later masters.
- [[si-en|四恩 / Four Kindnesses / 四恩（しおりん）]] — The Buddhist teaching on four debts of gratitude—to parents, teachers, sovereign, and sentient beings—that form the foundation of Buddhist ethical practice.
- [[thirty-seven-bodhiparamitas-an-shigao-commentary|Thirty-Seven Bodhiparamitas / 三十七品道品 / 三十七波羅蜜]] — A detailed analysis of the thirty-seven practices leading to enlightenment as expounded in An Shigao's commentary on the Yin Chi Ru Jing.
- [[thirty-seven-bodhiparamitas-an-shigao|Thirty-Seven Factors of Enlightenment / 三十七道品]] — A systematic classification of Buddhist practice teachings organized in progressive numerical categories (1-10), as presented in An Shigao's translation of the Long Discourses.
- [[thousand-lamp-body-offering-bodhisattva-practice|The King Who Lit a Thousand Lamps / 以身燃千燈之王]] — The Buddhist narrative of a king who sacrificed his own flesh to light a thousand lamps as the ultimate act of dedication to the Dharma.
- [[twelve-links-dependent-origination-an-shigao-commentary|Twelve Links of Dependent Origination / 十二因緣 / 十二縁起]] — Analysis of the twelve links of dependent origination as explained in An Shigao's commentary on the Yin Chi Ru Jing.
- [[white-cloth-golden-banner-two-brahmins-origin-sutra|White Cloth and Golden Banner Two Brahmins Origin Sutra / 白衣金幢二婆羅門緣起經]] — A Buddhist sutra recounting the renunciation of two Brahmins and presenting a Buddhist cosmology of human social origins.
- [[xianshou-wu-jiao|賢首五教 / Five Teachings of Xianshou / 賢首五教（けんじゅぎょう）]] — A five-tiered doctrinal classification system developed by Fazang (Xianshou) of the Huayan school, categorizing all Buddhist teachings from Hinayana to the highest Yogacara-Tathagatagarbha doctrines.

## Chinese-Buddhism-History

- [[an-shigao-seven-places-three-contemplations|An Shigao's Contribution: Seven Places and Three Contemplations / 安世高與七處三觀經]] — The Han dynasty translator An Shigao's systematic introduction of Buddhist meditative analysis through his translation of the Seven Places and Three Contemplations sutra.

## Chinese-Buddhist-Texts

- [[dacheng-bensheng-xindi-guanjing-kewen|大乘本生心地觀經淺註科文 / Commentary Outline on the Mahayana Mind-Ground Contemplation Sutra]] — A comprehensive structural outline and commentary classifying the contents of the Mahayana Sutra of Mind-Ground Contemplation into prefaces, main text, and circulation sections with detailed doctrinal divisions.
- [[moonlit-king-bodhisattva-sutra-yueguang-puti|Sutra of the Moonlight King (Moonlight Bodhisattva Sutra) / 佛說月光菩薩經]] — A Mahayana sutra describing the past life of the Buddha as Moonlight King, who attained bodhisattva awakening through the perfection of giving by donating his head to a brahmin.

## Chinese-Buddhist-Translation

- [[great-collection-dharma-gate-sutra|Great Collection Dharma Gate Sutra / 大集法門經]] — A Mahayana sutra presenting Buddhist teachings through systematic numerical enumeration from one to ten, taught by Śāriputra.

## Chinese-Classics

- [[confucian-sincerity-cheng|Sincerity (Cheng) in Confucianism / 誠]] — A core Confucian virtue representing authenticity, the metaphysical foundation of human nature, and the highest achievement of moral cultivation.
- [[dao-de-jing-silk-manuscript|Dao De Jing (Silk Manuscript) / 道德經帛書本 / 道德経帛書本]] — The Dao De Jing Silk Manuscript presents the earliest complete version of Laozi's text, with its distinctive chapter ordering placing virtue before the Way.
- [[doctrine-of-the-mean-(zhongyong)|Doctrine of the Mean (Zhongyong) / 中庸]] — A Confucian classic articulating the principle of equilibrium and moral self-cultivation through inner sincerity.
- [[erya-classic-chinese-glossary|Erya (Classic of Correct Rhymes) / 爾雅]] — The Erya is China's oldest comprehensive glossary, compiled during the Warring States-Han period, providing definitions of classical terms across categories with phonetic annotations.
- [[great-learning-daxue|The Great Learning / 大學]] — A foundational Confucian classic on self-cultivation and the investigation of things, forming part of the Four Books of Confucianism.
- [[li-ji-guan-yi-meaning-capping-rite|The Meaning of the Capping Rite / 禮記·冠義]] — A classical Confucian text from the Book of Rites explaining the ritual significance of the capping ceremony as the foundation of all ritual propriety and the gateway to adult moral responsibility.
- [[lijineize-rites-inner-principles|Inner Regulations (Neize) from the Book of Rites / 禮記內則]] — A Confucian chapter detailing domestic rituals, family conduct, gender-specific education, elderly care, and cooking methods for proper household governance.
- [[sun-tzu-art-of-war|Sun Tzu's Art of War / 孫子兵法 / 孫氏兵法]] — An ancient Chinese military treatise by Sun Tzu consisting of thirteen chapters covering strategic principles, tactics, intelligence gathering, and the philosophy of warfare.
- [[tai-shang-gan-ying-pian|Tai Shang Gan Ying Pian / 太上感應篇]] — A foundational Daoist moral treatise on karmic retribution, emphasizing that fortune and misfortune are not arbitrary but arise from one's own actions.

## Chinese-Ethics

- [[benevolence|Benevolence / 仁]] — Discusses the foundational role of benevolence in Confucian ethics and its implications for interpersonal relationships and governance.

## Chinese-Fable

- [[yu-gong-yi-shan-yugong-moves-mountains|Yu Gong Moves the Mountains / 愚公移山]] — A famous Chinese fable from Liezi about an old man who decided to move two large mountains blocking his village, demonstrating the power of persistence and collective effort.

## Chinese-Military-Thought

- [[mozi-miscellaneous-defense-zashou|Miscellaneous Defense (雜守) / 墨子·雜守]] — A Mozi chapter detailing comprehensive urban defense strategies against siege warfare, covering tactical formations, garrison organization, supply management, and beacon communication systems.
- [[san-lue-three-strategies|Three Strategies / 三略]] — A classical Chinese military treatise divided into three volumes (Upper, Middle, Lower) addressing military command, statecraft, and governance principles.

## Chinese-Mythology

- [[san-shi-shen-three-corpses|Three Corpses / 三尸神]] — The Three Corpses (三尸神) are celestial observers dwelling within the human body who record sins and report them to heaven during the Gengshen day, playing a central role in Daoist karmic surveillance systems.
- [[wu-zhi-five-fungi-baopuzi|Five Fungi (五芝) in Baopuzi / 抱朴子五芝]] — The classification and effects of five types of fungi (石芝、木芝、草芝、肉芝、菌芝) for immortality in Daoist alchemy.

## Chinese-Philosophy

- [[bagua-formation-trigrams-yijing|Eight Trigrams Formation / 八卦成列]] — The philosophical principle of how the eight trigrams are arranged to manifest all phenomena in the Yijing
- [[baopuzi-critique-false-deities-folk-religion|Bao Puzi Chapter 9: Critique of False Deities and Folk Religion / 抱朴子卷九：批判淫祀邪教]] — Ge Hong's philosophical critique of fraudulent religious practices, false deities, and the importance of self-cultivation over external ritual worship.
- [[beigongzi-ximenzi-virtue-fate-liezi|Beigongzi and Ximenzi — Virtue and Fate in Liezi / 北宮子與西門子：德厚命薄]] — A philosophical dialogue exploring how virtue (德) and fate (命) operate independently, with East Guo Master's revelation that Beigongzi has厚德薄命 while Ximenzi has厚命薄德.
- [[benevolent-government-ren-zheng|Benevolent Government / 仁政 / 仁政]] — Mencius's political philosophy advocating that rulers should govern through benevolence and moral virtue rather than coercion and punishment.
- [[bo-chengzi-gao-zhuangzi|Bo Chengzi Gao / 伯成子高]] — A hermit from the Zhuangzi who refused to serve as a feudal lord, critiquing the shift from reward-free governance to punitive systems.
- [[bu-shang-wei-ben-principle-cultivation|Non-Injury as Foundation in Cultivation / 不傷為本]] — The fundamental principle in Daoist cultivation that protecting the body and preserving qi from damage is the essential foundation for longevity and eventual immortality.
- [[bu-xiang-ai|Non-Mutual Love / 不相愛]] — Mozi's concept identifying the lack of mutual love as the fundamental cause of all social chaos and disorder.
- [[cautious-speech-conduct-liezi-shuofu|Caution in Speech and Conduct / 慎言慎行]] — The philosophical principle from Liezi's Shuofu chapter on how careful speech and conduct shape one's destiny through cause and effect.
- [[chongyan-revered-discourse-zhuangzi|Chongyan (Revered Discourse) in Zhuangzi / 重言（莊子）]] — "Revered Discourse" (重言) — the second of Zhuangzi's three discourse modes, quoting ancient sages and elders to lend authority to philosophical teachings.
- [[confucian-sincerity-cheng|Sincerity (Cheng) in Confucianism / 誠]] — A core Confucian virtue representing authenticity, the metaphysical foundation of human nature, and the highest achievement of moral cultivation.
- [[confucius-analects|Analects of Confucius / 论语]] — A collection of sayings and ideas attributed to the Chinese philosopher Confucius.
- [[confucius-etiquette-xiang-dang|Confucius's Etiquette in Public Life / 孔子乡党礼仪]] — Chapter 10 of the Analects describing Confucius's formal behavior and ritual propriety in various social contexts including village, court, ceremonies, and interactions with different ranks of people.
- [[confucius-western-saint-liezi|Confucius and the Western Saint (西方聖者) / 西方聖者]] — A Liezi account of Confucius making an enigmatic reference to "a saint in the west" who rules without governing, speaks without persuasion, and transforms without coercion.
- [[dao-ben-ru-mo-dao-as-root-confucianism-as-branch|Dao as Root, Confucianism as Branch / 道本儒末]] — A philosophical doctrine from Baopuzi asserting that the Dao is the foundation while Confucianism represents its derivative applications.
- [[dao-de-jing-complete|Dao De Jing (Complete) / 道德經]] — A comprehensive classical Chinese text of Daoist philosophy attributed to Laozi, preserved in multiple manuscript traditions and annotated through extensive commentary lineages across Chinese dynastic history.
- [[dao-the-way-taoism|Dao (The Way) / 道]] — The fundamental Taoist concept of Dao (The Way), the ultimate reality and principle underlying the universe.
- [[doctrine-of-the-mean-(zhongyong)|Doctrine of the Mean (Zhongyong) / 中庸]] — A Confucian classic articulating the principle of equilibrium and moral self-cultivation through inner sincerity.
- [[doctrine-of-the-mean-zhongyong|Doctrine of the Mean (Zhongyong) / 中庸]] — A Confucian classic teaching the principle of balanced moderation and harmonious equilibrium as the foundation of virtue and sagehood.
- [[dongmen-wu-grieflessness|Dongmen Wu's Grieflessness / 東門吳之無憂]] — The story of Dongmen Wu, who remained unmoved by his son's death because he had previously been without a son and felt no loss.
- [[dream-reality-self-guan-yin-zi|The Nature of Self and Reality in Guan Yin Zi / 關尹子中的自我與真實]] — An exploration of the philosophical arguments in Chapter 6 of Guan Yin Zi concerning the distinction between self and other, dreams and reality, and the mutable nature of form.
- [[fengshi-son-perceptual-inversion-liezi|The Son of Feng Clan with Perceptual Inversion / 逢氏之子迷罔]] — A story from Liezi about a son who suffers from inverted perceptions, mistaking sweet for bitter, white for black, and right for wrong.
- [[five-elements-theory-constancy-transformation|Five Elements Theory: Constancy and Transformation / 五行常變論]] — The theory of five elements (water, fire, wood, metal, earth) as constant yet infinitely variable principles in Chinese cosmology and philosophy.
- [[force-fate-debate-liezi|Force and Fate Debate / 力命之辯]] — The philosophical dialogue between Force (力) and Fate (命) exploring whether human effort or destiny determines life outcomes.
- [[four-beginnings-si-duan|Four Beginnings / 四端 / 四端説]] — Mencius's theory that human nature contains four sprouts of virtue that can develop into benevolence, rightness, propriety, and wisdom.
- [[four-kingdoms-sleep-dream-liezi|Four Kingdoms of Dream and Reality / 四國夢覺]] — A philosophical passage from Liezi describing four kingdoms with contrasting relationships to sleep, dreams, and reality.
- [[four-permutations-fate-liezi|Four Permutations of Fate / 四可之命]] — The doctrine of four possible outcomes regarding life and death, each potentially either heavenly blessing or punishment depending on alignment with natural order.
- [[gengsang-chu-zhuangzi|Gengsang Chu Chapter in Zhuangzi / 莊子·庚桑楚]] — A chapter in Zhuangzi featuring the disciple Gengsang Chu's philosophy of preserving life, avoiding fame, and the Daoist concept of the "hygiene classic."
- [[gong-yibo-strength-liezi|Gong Yibo's Humility About Strength (公儀伯之力) / 公儀伯之力]] — A Liezi anecdote about Gong Yibo explaining true strength through the example of his master Shang Qiu, who possessed invincible power yet never used it.
- [[great-learning-daxue|The Great Learning / 大學]] — A foundational Confucian classic on self-cultivation and the investigation of things, forming part of the Four Books of Confucianism.
- [[great-qi-haoran-zhi-qi|Great Qi / 浩然之氣 / 浩然之気]] — Mencius's concept of "great qi" - a cultivated spiritual vital energy that fills the universe and empowers moral accomplishment.
- [[guan-bao-friendship-liezi|Guan Zhong and Bao Shuya Friendship / 管鮑之交]] — The paradigmatic friendship between Guan Zhong and Bao Shuya, reinterpreted by Liezi as an example of fate determining social outcomes rather than personal virtue.
- [[guan-yinzi-chapter-five-mind-intention-nature|Guan Yinzi Chapter Five: Mind, Intention, and Nature / 關尹子第五章：心、意與性]] — Chapter 5 of Guan Yinzi explores the relationship between mind (心), intention (意), emotions (情), and original nature (性), presenting a sophisticated psychological framework that distinguishes between the unchanging mind and transforming intentions.
- [[guan-yinzi-chapter-six-self-cultivation|Guanyinzi Chapter Six: Self-Cultivation and the Nature of Self / 關尹子第六章：修养与自我本性]] — Chapter Six of Guanyinzi explores the nature of self through dream analysis, form transformation, and the dissolution of subject-object distinctions, presenting core Daoist concepts of self-cultivation.
- [[guan-yinzi-chapter-three-sage-way|Guān Yǐnzǐ Chapter Three: The Way of the Sage / 關尹子第三章：聖人之道]] — Chapter 3 of the Daoist classic Guān Yǐnzǐ explores the sage's governance through non-action, the doctrine of non-self, and the inexpressibility of the Dao.
- [[guanyinzi-chapter-eight|Guanyinzi Chapter 8 / 關尹子第八篇]] — Chapter 8 of the Daoist text Guanyinzi discusses the ineffable nature of the Dao, the five-element transformations, the heart-mind as creator of all things, and the sage's unity with Heaven.
- [[guanyinzi-chapter-five-mind-transformation|Guanyinzi Chapter Five: Mind and Cosmological Transformation / 關尹子第五章：心與造化]] — Chapter 5 of Guanyinzi explores the nature of the mind (心), its interactions with spirits and external objects, and the sage's mastery over mental transformation to transcend form and qi.
- [[guanyinzi-chapter-nine|Guanyinzi Chapter Nine: On Medicine / 關尹子第九章：藥者雜治]] — Chapter 9 of Guanyinzi presents the "medicine" metaphor for spiritual practice, discussing how the sage applies various remedies to correct imbalances between extremes.
- [[guanyinzi-chapter-seven-transformation|Chapter Seven: Transformation (化) in Guanyinzi / 關尹子第七章：化]] — Chapter 7 of Guanyinzi explores the philosophy of transformation (化),阐發道化萬物、聖人任化的深層道理.
- [[hao-bridge-debate-fish-happiness|The Hao Bridge Debate / 濠梁之辯]] — The famous philosophical exchange between Zhuangzi and Hui Zi about whether one can know a fish's happiness, exploring questions of consciousness and knowledge.
- [[investigating-things-extending-knowledge-gewu-zhizhi|Investigating Things and Extending Knowledge / 格物致知]] — The foundational step in Confucian self-cultivation involving the investigation of things and extension of knowledge, a concept central to both Neo-Confucian and Ming-era philosophical debates.
- [[jian-ai|Universal Love (兼愛) / 兼愛]] — The Mohist principle advocating equal care for all people without distinction, considered the foundation of Mozi's ethical philosophy.
- [[jing-shen-hun-po-essence-spirit-soul|Essence, Spirit, Soul, and Corporeal Soul (精神魂魄) / 精神魂魄說]] — A Taoist doctrine from Guanyinzi Chapter 4 explaining the four fundamental spiritual faculties: essence (精), spirit (神), soul (魂), and corporeal soul (魄), their cosmic origins, and their relationship to the Five Elements.
- [[jiu-fang-gao-horse-divination-liezi|Jiu Fang Gao's Horse Divination / 九方皋相馬]] — A parable about seeing essential nature beyond superficial appearance, exemplified through horse divination that prioritizes inner truth over external signs.
- [[liji-aigong-wen-duke-ai-inquires|Duke Ai Inquires (Liji Chapter) / 禮記·哀公問]] — A Confucian dialogue between Duke Ai of Lu and Confucius on ritual propriety, governance, and the cultivation of the self through filial conduct.
- [[mengzi-seven-chapters-gongsun-chou-part-two|Mencius: Gongsun Chou Part Two / 孟子·公孫丑下]] — A comprehensive wiki article covering the second chapter of Mencius, including analysis of its fourteen sections on political philosophy, governance principles, and historical events.
- [[mengzi|Mencius / 孟子]] — Mencius (c. 372–289 BCE) was the most prominent Confucian philosopher after Confucius, known for his doctrine of the innate goodness of human nature.
- [[mind-solidified-form-dissolved-liezi|Mind Solidified and Form Dissolved (心凝形釋) / 心凝形釋]] — A Liezi description of advanced spiritual attainment where the mind becomes solidified while the physical body dissolves, representing ultimate unity of consciousness and form.
- [[ming-gui-xia-ghost-spirit-doctrine|Demonstrating the Existence of Ghosts Part 2 / 明鬼下]] — A Mohist chapter demonstrating the existence and moral function of ghosts and spirits, arguing that belief in supernatural reward and punishment is essential for social order.
- [[ministerial-responsibility|Ministerial Responsibility / 臣責]] — A concept in Chinese political philosophy concerning the duties and obligations of ministers toward their rulers.
- [[mozi-da-qu|Mozi Da Qu (Great Adoption) / 墨子·大取]] — An analysis of the Mozi chapter "Da Qu" which discusses the methodology of moral weighing between benefit and harm, including principles of self-sacrifice for the world.
- [[mozi-fayi-standard-law|Mozi's Standard of Law (法儀) / 墨子法儀]] — Mozi argues that all governance requires a standard or model, and that Heaven (天) rather than parents, teachers, or rulers should serve as the ultimate ethical benchmark.
- [[mozi-fei-gong-zhong-against-attack-middle|Mozi Fei Gong Zhong / 墨子·非攻中]] — Chapter 18 of the Mozi, continuing the critique of aggressive warfare with detailed economic analysis and historical examples demonstrating the futility of conquest.
- [[mozi-fei-ming-against-fatalism|Against Fatalism (非命上) / 墨子非命思想]] — Mozi's philosophical refutation of fatalism and the doctrine of predetermined destiny, arguing for human agency and the Three Standards methodology.
- [[mozi-fei-yue-shang-against-music-upper|Mozi Against Music Part I (非樂上) — Mohist Critique of Music and Governance]] — Mozi's philosophical argument against elaborate music, contending that rulers' expenditure on music harms the people's welfare and disrupts governance, based on the principle of promoting world benefit while eliminating world harm.
- [[mozi-gong-meng-chapter|Mozi - Gong Meng Chapter / 墨子·公孟]] — A philosophical dialogue between Mozi and the Confucian scholar Gong Meng covering debates on proactive moral speech, ritual propriety, fate, and the unity of words and actions.
- [[mozi-gongshu-dialogue-chapter|Mozi Gongshu Chapter / 墨子公輸篇]] — A chapter from the Mozi text describing Mozi's debate with Gongshu Ban and his dissuasion of Chu's attack on Song through logical argument and a military defense demonstration.
- [[mozi-gui-yi-valuing-righteousness|Mozi Chapter on Valuing Righteousness / 墨子·貴義]] — A chapter from the Mozi emphasizing righteousness as the highest value, contrasting with the utility of name-based versus actual selection, and demonstrating Mozi's political teachings through various encounters.
- [[mozi-heaven-will-tianzhi|Heaven's Will (天志) in Mozi's Philosophy / 墨子天志哲學]] — Mozi's concept of 天志 (Heaven's Will) establishes Heaven as the supreme moral authority that desires righteousness and punishes unrighteousness, serving as the cosmic foundation for political legitimacy and ethical conduct.
- [[mozi-illuminating-ghosts-ming-gui|Mozi - Illuminating Ghosts (Ming Gui) / 墨子·明鬼]] — Mozi's chapter arguing for the existence of ghosts and spirits who reward virtue and punish vice, using historical evidence and experiential verification.
- [[mozi-jie-yong-utility-frugality|Mozi on Utility (節用) — The Principle of Frugality in Mohist Governance / 墨子節用思想——兼愛天下的功利原則]] — Mozi's "On Frugality" (節用) chapter outlines the principle that rulers should only employ resources for practical utility, eliminating wasteful expenditures to maximize social benefit and national strength.
- [[mozi-jie-zang-frugal-burial|Mozi on Frugal Burial (節葬) / 墨子節葬]] — Mozi's critique of excessive burial practices and prolonged mourning, arguing for simple burials based on the examples of ancient sage kings.
- [[mozi-jie-zang-funeral-simplicity|Mozi's Funeral Simplicity / 墨子節葬思想]] — Mozi's philosophical argument against elaborate funerals and prolonged mourning, advocating simple burial practices based on utilitarian principles.
- [[mozi-preparing-against-elevated-attacks|Mozi on Preparing Against Elevated Attacks / 墨子備高臨]] — A chapter from the Mozi detailing Mohist defensive strategies against enemy siege towers and elevated attack positions, including technical specifications for repeating crossbow carts.
- [[mozi-rejecting-confucians-fei-ru|Mozi's Rejection of Confucians (非儒下) / 墨子·非儒下]] — A Mohist critique of Confucian ethics, mourning rituals, fatalism, and Confucius's political conduct through detailed arguments and historical anecdotes.
- [[mozi-sage-kings-burial-model|The Sage Kings' Burial Model in Mozi / 墨子聖王葬埋之法]] — Mozi's use of the ancient sage kings (Yao, Shun, Yu) as historical examples for proper burial practices, contrasting with contemporary lavish funerals.
- [[mozi-seven-calamities-qi-huan|Seven Calamities in Mozi / 墨子七患]] — A Mohist analysis of the seven types of calamities that threaten state survival, emphasizing preparedness, agricultural foundation, and virtuous governance.
- [[mozi-suoran-on-influence|Mozi On Dyeing / 墨子·所染]] — A Mozi chapter using the silk-dyeing metaphor to illustrate how one's associates determine moral character and political fortune.
- [[mozi-three-debates-music-governance|Mozi's Three Debates on Music and Governance / 墨子三辯]] — A philosophical dialogue in the Mozi examining why sage-kings did not engage in music, and the inverse relationship between musical complexity and governance effectiveness.
- [[mozi-upper-canon-jing-shang|Mozi Upper Canon (經上) / 墨子·經上]] — A foundational Mohist philosophical text defining core concepts including knowledge, virtue, cause, and methodology through systematic binary definitions.
- [[mozi-xiaoqu-logical-methodology|Mozi's Logical Methodology / 墨子逻辑方法论 / 墨子論理方法論]] — A systematic analysis of the logical and dialectical methodology presented in the "Xiaoqu" chapter of Mozi, including the theory of names and realities, argumentation methods, and principles of correct reasoning.
- [[mozi-xiaoqu-logical-methods|Xiaoqu (Minor Selections) - Mozi's Logical Methods / 墨子小取——論理方法]] — A chapter from the Mozi presenting a systematic analysis of dialectical reasoning methods including analogy, parallelism, citing, deduction, and their proper applications.
- [[mozi-xiaoqu-mohist-logic|Mozi Xiaoqu: On Logical Reasoning / 墨子小取：論辯說之法]] — The Xiaoqu chapter of Mozi presents a systematic exposition of Mohist logic, including seven types of reasoning and epistemological principles for philosophical debate.
- [[mozi-xiu-shen-self-cultivation|Mozi's Self-Cultivation / 墨子修身]] — A chapter from the Mozi discussing the fundamentals of self-cultivation, emphasizing courage, action, and integrity as the essential roots of moral cultivation.
- [[mozijing|Mozijing / 墨經]] — The "Classic of Mozi" - core philosophical text of Mohism containing the school's major doctrines and logical treatises.
- [[prince-ming-zhangshan-gongsun-long-liezi|Prince Ming of Zhongshan and Gongsun Long (中山公子牟) / 中山公子牟]] — A Liezi account of a philosophical debate between the nobleman Prince Ming and his associates regarding the dialectician Gongsun Long and his logical paradoxes.
- [[pure-qi-transformation-hunqi-bianhua|Pure Qi Transformation / 純氣變化]] — A Daoist concept from Guanyinzi describing how pure qi (氣) can transform all things in the universe, including reversing natural laws and animating inanimate objects.
- [[qiushui-autumn-floods-zhuangzi|Autumn Floods / 秋水]] — Chapter 17 of Zhuangzi featuring the philosophical dialogue between the River God and Sea God on relativism, perspective, and the limits of human understanding.
- [[self-generating-life-death|Self-Generating Life and Death / 自生自死]] — The Liezi doctrine that life, death, prosperity, and poverty arise spontaneously from fate, not from human control.
- [[shang-tong-upper-unity-mozi|Shang Tong (Upper Unity) / 尚同]] — Shang Tong is Mozi's political doctrine advocating hierarchical unity of thought under proper authority to achieve social order.
- [[shang-xian-exalting-worthy|Exalting the Worthy (尚賢) / 尚賢]] — A core Mohist political doctrine emphasizing that rulers should promote individuals of virtue and talent regardless of their social background, making worthy officials the foundation of good governance.
- [[true-person-without-dreams-liezi|The True Person Without Dreams / 古之真人其寢不夢]] — The Liezi teaching on the perfected sage (真人) who, through spiritual cultivation, transcends the ordinary distinction between dreaming and waking, achieving a state of pure consciousness untroubled by illusions.
- [[ultimate-wandering-observation-liezi|Ultimate Wandering and Observation (至游至觀) / 至游至觀]] — A Liezi philosophical concept about the highest form of spiritual wandering and observation, transcending attachment to external objects.
- [[understanding-heaven-knowing-fate-liezi|Understanding Heaven and Knowing Fate (樂天知命) / 樂天知命]] — A Liezi philosophical concept about rejoicing in Heaven's will and knowing one's fate, evolving from conventional wisdom to transcendent understanding.
- [[wenzi-text|Wenzi (The Book of Master Wen) / 文子]] — An ancient Daoist text presenting Laozi's philosophy through a dialogue format, attributed to a disciple of Laozi, covering the nature of the Dao, non-action governance, and the ideal sage.
- [[woodcutter-dream-deer-liezi|The Woodcutter's Dream of the Deer / 薪者夢鹿]] — A philosophical story from Liezi about a woodcounter who dreams of catching a deer, leading to a legal dispute about the nature of reality and dream.
- [[wu-yuan-five-origins-guan-yin-zi|The Five Origins (五元) in Guān Yǐnzǐ / 關尹子五元論]] — An exploration of the Five Origins cosmology (天、命、神、元、道) presented in Guān Yǐnzǐ, a Taoist text emphasizing the omnipresence and indivisibility of the cosmic principles.
- [[wuyong-zhi-yong-usefulness-of-uselessness|The Usefulness of Uselessness / 無用之用]] — A central Zhuangzi parable about the useless tree that survives because it has no use to humans, illustrating the Daoist principle that apparent uselessness may be the highest utility.
- [[xiao-jing-classic-of-filial-piety|Classic of Filial Piety / 孝經]] — The Classic of Filial Piety (Xiaojing) is a Confucian text outlining the principles and practices of filial piety, existing in two main textual traditions.
- [[xinzhai-heart-fasting|Heart Fasting / 心齋]] — A Zhuangzi concept of spiritual purification through emptiness of the heart-mind, taught by Confucius to Yan Hui as the path to navigate the human world.
- [[xuandao-mysterious-way|Xuandao (The Mysterious Way) / 玄道]] — The supreme metaphysical principle "玄" (Xuan/Mystery) discussed in Baopuzi, described as the origin of nature and the great source of all myriad things, transcending physical existence.
- [[yan-person-return-homeland-liezi|The Yan Person Returning Home / 燕人歸國]] — A story from Liezi about a man from Yan who was raised in Chu and became confused about his identity when returning to his homeland.
- [[yang-zhu-philosophy-liezi|Yang Zhu's Philosophy in Liezi / 楊朱篇的哲學思想]] — Yang Zhu's individualist and hedonist philosophy as presented in the Liezi, emphasizing self-preservation, the brevity of life, and rejection of fame and social obligations.
- [[yu-dwelling-abode-daoist-concept|Yu (Dwelling/Abode) in Daoist Philosophy / 寓（道家哲學中的棲居）]] — The concept of "寓" (dwelling/abode) as the Dao's manifestation in all things, from Chapter 2 of Guǎn Yǐnzǐ.
- [[zhihou-yan-chengzi-spiritual-progression-zhuangzi|Yan Chengzi's Nine-Year Spiritual Progression / 顏成子游九年大妙]] — The account of Yan Chengzi You's nine-year spiritual transformation from worldly refinement to ultimate enlightenment, as recorded in Zhuangzi.
- [[zhili-qixing-deformed-ones-zhuangzi|The Deformed Ones / 支離其形]] — Zhuangzi's celebration of physically deformed individuals who, excluded from worldly usefulness, survive and prosper—the paradox of form versus spirit in Daoist philosophy.
- [[zhuangzi-fables-parables-yuyan|Zhuangzi Chapter 27: Fables / 莊子·寓言]] — The 27th chapter of Zhuangzi introducing three types of discourse—fables, elders' sayings, and spontaneous speech—to convey Daoist teachings through external examples and natural patterns.
- [[zhuangzi-gengsang-chu-chapter|Gengsang Chu Chapter (庚桑楚) / 庚桑楚篇]] — Chapter 23 of Zhuangzi featuring the disciple Gengsang Chu's philosophy of self-preservation, his dialogue with Laozi on the "hygiene of life," and profound discussions of being and non-being.
- [[zhuangzi-heaven-earth-chapter|Zhuangzi Chapter on Heaven and Earth / 莊子·天地]] — A key chapter from Zhuangzi exploring the nature of the Way, governance through non-action, and the corruption of innate nature through artificiality.
- [[zhuangzi-ke-yi-chapter|Kè Yì (Cultivating Deliberate Purpose) / 刻意]] — Zhuangzi Chapter 15 explores five types of self-cultivation and advocates for the sage's path of tranquility, simplicity, and non-deliberate action.
- [[zhuangzi-shanxing-chapter|Shanxing (Rectifying Nature) Chapter in Zhuangzi / 莊子·繕性]] — A chapter discussing the rectification of nature through stillness and naturalness, contrasting worldly learning with returning to original spontaneity, and analyzing the historical decline of the Dao.
- [[zhuangzi-supreme-joy-zhi-le|Supreme Joy (至樂) in Zhuangzi / 莊子至樂篇]] — Zhuangzi's philosophical exploration of true happiness beyond worldly pleasures, arguing that ultimate joy transcends conventional notions of joy itself.
- [[zhuangzi-turtle-story-rejection|Zhuangzi's Turtle Story / 莊子曳尾塗中]] — The famous anecdote of Zhuangzi refusing official service from the King of Chu, choosing instead to drag his tail in the mud—a classic expression of Daoist values.
- [[zhuangzi-ying-di-wang|Zhuangzi Chapter 7: Responses of Kings / 莊子·應帝王]] — Chapter 7 of Zhuangzi discusses the qualities of the ideal ruler and the principle of non-action in governance, featuring the famous allegory of Chaos (渾沌).
- [[义|Righteousness / 义]] — A fundamental Confucian virtue representing moral righteousness, appropriate conduct, and the principle of doing what is right.
- [[仁者|仁者 / Benevolent Person]] — A person who has cultivated and embodies the Confucian virtue of benevolence (仁), serving as a moral exemplar.
- [[生子憂患死於安樂|Birth through Suffering, Death through Comfort / 生子憂患死於安樂]] — A philosophical concept from Liezi expressing that hardship produces growth while comfort leads to decline.

## Chinese-Political-Philosophy

- [[mozi-seven-calamities-qi-huan|Seven Calamities in Mozi / 墨子七患]] — A Mohist analysis of the seven types of calamities that threaten state survival, emphasizing preparedness, agricultural foundation, and virtuous governance.
- [[nong-zhan-agricultural-war|Agricultural War Doctrine / 農戰]] — A Legalist doctrine from the Book of Lord Shang emphasizing the unification of agricultural production and military service as the twin pillars of state power.

## Chinese-Religion

- [[baopuzi-volume-19-daoist-scriptures-catalog|Baopuzi Volume 19: Catalog of Daoist Texts / 抱朴子卷十九道書目錄]] — Ge Hong's comprehensive catalog of over 180 Daoist texts including Three Sovereigns Inner Text, Five Peaks True Form Map, talismans, alchemy scripts, and esoteric practices, as recorded from his teacher Zheng Jun.
- [[five-peaks-true-form-map-wuyue-zhenxing-tu|Five Peaks True Form Map / 五嶽真形圖]] — A most sacred Taoist talisman text described in Baopuzi as requiring blood oaths, forty-year transmission cycles, and possessing powers to ward off evil, heal diseases, cross waters, and reveal hidden knowledge.
- [[shan-e-bao-ying-karmic-retribution|Shan E Bao Ying / 善惡報應 (善悪因果応報)]] — The doctrine of karmic retribution in Chinese religious traditions, holding that good and evil deeds generate corresponding rewards and punishments from celestial forces.

## Chinese-Ritual

- [[li-ji-ben-sang-hurrying-to-mourning|Rushing to Mourning (Ben Sang) / 禮記·奔喪]] — The Book of Rites describes the ritual procedures for a son rushing home upon learning of a parent's death, including immediate response protocols, travel customs, and mourning ceremonies.
- [[sangfu-xiaoji-liji|Sangfu Xiaoji (Minor Records of Mourning Dress) / 喪服小記]] — A chapter from the Book of Rites detailing mourning dress regulations, mourning periods, and ritual protocols for various kinship relationships.

## Chinese-Ritual-Theory

- [[cheng-qing-er-li-wen-ritual-emotion-alignment|Establishing Ritual Based on Emotion / 稱情而立文]] — A Confucian ritual principle that proper ceremonial forms should be established according to genuine human emotions and feelings, serving as external expressions of internal grief.

## Chinese-Rituals

- [[sang-da-ji-funeral-rituals-liji|Sang Da Ji: Major Records of Mourning / 喪大記：喪禮大典]] — A chapter from the Liji detailing hierarchical funeral procedures for rulers, ministers, and commoners, including encoffinement rites, mourning staff protocols, and deathbed rituals.

## Chinese-Texts

- [[mozi-ciguo-refraining-from-excesses|Mozi - Refraining from Excesses (辭過) / 墨子·辭過]] — A chapter from the Mozi examining how ancient sage-kings established proper standards for five essential domains of life—dwelling, clothing, food, transportation, and marriage—contrasting their frugal governance with the excesses of contemporary rulers.
- [[xiao-jing-classic-of-filial-piety|Classic of Filial Piety / 孝經]] — The Classic of Filial Piety (Xiaojing) is a Confucian text outlining the principles and practices of filial piety, existing in two main textual traditions.

## Chinese-Thought

- [[儒家|儒家 / 儒家]] — Confucianism - a foundational Chinese philosophical tradition centered on ethics, virtue, and social harmony.

## City-Defense

- [[mozi-banner-system-siege-defense|Mozi's Banner System for Siege Defense / 墨子旗幟制度]] — Mozi's systematic color-coded banner system for identifying defenders, materials, and military roles during siege warfare.
- [[mozi-defending-city-walls-beichengmen|Defending City Walls (Mozi) / 墨子備城門]] — A Mohist military defense treatise detailing systematic strategies for city wall protection against twelve siege methods, emphasizing preparation, material readiness, and coordinated defender response.
- [[mozi-miscellaneous-defense-zashou|Miscellaneous Defense (雜守) / 墨子·雜守]] — A Mozi chapter detailing comprehensive urban defense strategies against siege warfare, covering tactical formations, garrison organization, supply management, and beacon communication systems.
- [[mozi-preparing-against-tunnel-attacks|Preparing Against Tunnel Attacks (Mozi Chapter on Underground Defense) / 墨子備穴]] — A defensive warfare chapter from the Mozi text detailing strategies to detect and counter enemy tunneling attacks under city walls using acoustic detection, smoke熏攻, and structural defenses.
- [[tu-men-tunnel-gates-city-defense|Tumen (Tunnel Gates) / 突門（城門突入口）]] — Tumen were hidden tunnel gate passages built into city walls at intervals of every hundred paces, designed as defensive traps against underground siege attacks using kilns, bellows, and smoke.

## City-Fortification

- [[mozi-defending-city-walls-beichengmen|Defending City Walls (Mozi) / 墨子備城門]] — A Mohist military defense treatise detailing systematic strategies for city wall protection against twelve siege methods, emphasizing preparation, material readiness, and coordinated defender response.
- [[mozi-water-defense-strategies|Mozi's Water Defense Strategies / 墨子備水戰術]] — A chapter from the Mozi detailing defensive preparations and tactical responses against water attacks on fortified cities, including drainage systems, naval organization, and coordinated counterattacks.

## City-Wall-Defense

- [[mozi-preparing-against-elevated-attacks|Mozi on Preparing Against Elevated Attacks / 墨子備高臨]] — A chapter from the Mozi detailing Mohist defensive strategies against enemy siege towers and elevated attack positions, including technical specifications for repeating crossbow carts.

## Classical Chinese Thought

- [[human-nature-mencius-debate|The Mencian Debate on Human Nature / 孟子人性论辩]] — A philosophical examination of the debate between Mencius and Gaozi regarding the nature of human beings, including key analogies and arguments.

## Classical Chinese Literature

- [[mengzi|Mencius / 孟子]] — Mencius (c. 372–289 BCE) was the most prominent Confucian philosopher after Confucius, known for his doctrine of the innate goodness of human nature.

## Classical Text

- [[關尹子|關尹子 / Guanyinzi]] — A Daoist text attributed to Yin Xi, presenting teachings on sage governance and cosmic transformation

## Classical Texts

- [[guanyinzi-chapter-eight|Guanyinzi Chapter 8 / 關尹子第八篇]] — Chapter 8 of the Daoist text Guanyinzi discusses the ineffable nature of the Dao, the five-element transformations, the heart-mind as creator of all things, and the sage's unity with Heaven.

## Classical-Canon

- [[han-dynasty-mencius-reception|Han Dynasty Reception of Mencius / 汉代孟子接受史]] — Historical process of Mencius's recognition and preservation during the Han dynasty

## Classical-Chinese

- [[erya-classic-chinese-glossary|Erya (Classic of Correct Rhymes) / 爾雅]] — The Erya is China's oldest comprehensive glossary, compiled during the Warring States-Han period, providing definitions of classical terms across categories with phonetic annotations.
- [[guanyinzi-chapter-nine|Guanyinzi Chapter Nine: On Medicine / 關尹子第九章：藥者雜治]] — Chapter 9 of Guanyinzi presents the "medicine" metaphor for spiritual practice, discussing how the sage applies various remedies to correct imbalances between extremes.
- [[liutao-six-secret-strategies|Six Secret Strategies / 六韜 / 六韜]] — An ancient Chinese military treatise traditionally attributed to Jiang Ziya, consisting of six sections covering civil and military governance strategies.
- [[mozi-illuminating-ghosts-ming-gui|Mozi - Illuminating Ghosts (Ming Gui) / 墨子·明鬼]] — Mozi's chapter arguing for the existence of ghosts and spirits who reward virtue and punish vice, using historical evidence and experiential verification.
- [[mozi-upper-canon-jing-shang|Mozi Upper Canon (經上) / 墨子·經上]] — A foundational Mohist philosophical text defining core concepts including knowledge, virtue, cause, and methodology through systematic binary definitions.
- [[mozi-xiaoqu-mohist-logic|Mozi Xiaoqu: On Logical Reasoning / 墨子小取：論辯說之法]] — The Xiaoqu chapter of Mozi presents a systematic exposition of Mohist logic, including seven types of reasoning and epistemological principles for philosophical debate.

## Classical-Chinese-Buddhism

- [[shi-men-tong-pan-ten-gates-framework|Ten Gates Framework / 十門通判]] — A methodological framework for sutra interpretation consisting of ten categories, originating from the Huayan school and used for systematic Buddhist textual analysis.

## Classical-Chinese-Philosophy

- [[benevolence|Benevolence / 仁]] — Discusses the foundational role of benevolence in Confucian ethics and its implications for interpersonal relationships and governance.
- [[doctrine-of-the-mean-(zhongyong)|Doctrine of the Mean (Zhongyong) / 中庸]] — A Confucian classic articulating the principle of equilibrium and moral self-cultivation through inner sincerity.
- [[great-learning-daxue|The Great Learning / 大學]] — A foundational Confucian classic on self-cultivation and the investigation of things, forming part of the Four Books of Confucianism.
- [[mengzi-four-beginnings-siduan|Four Beginnings (四端) / 四端說]] — Mencius's doctrine that human nature contains four innate moral sprouts: compassion, shame, deference, and judgment.
- [[mengzi-gaozi-debate|The Mencius-Gao Zi Debate on Human Nature / 孟子與告子之人性辯論]] — A philosophical exchange between Mencius and Gao Zi exploring whether human nature is morally neutral or inherently good.
- [[mengzi-losing-original-heart|Losing and Seeking the Original Heart / 放心]] — Mencius's concept of "fang xin" - the loss of one's innate moral consciousness and the imperative to recover it through learning.
- [[mengzi-seven-chapters-structural-analysis|Mencius Seven Chapters / 孟子七篇結構]] — Systematic analysis of the seven-chapter structure of Mencius and its philosophical significance
- [[willow-cup-metaphor-gaozi|Willow-Cup Metaphor / 杞柳桮棬]] — Gaozi's philosophical metaphor comparing human nature to willow wood that must be coerced into artificial forms, critiqued by Mencius.

## Classical-Chinese-Text

- [[lijji-fang-ji-ritual-prevention|Fang Ji - Prevention Through Ritual in the Book of Rites / 禮記·坊記——以禮坊民]] — A classical Confucian chapter explaining how ritual propriety (禮) serves as a "dyke" (坊) to prevent moral corruption, social disorder, and improper conduct in human relations.
- [[san-lue-three-strategies|Three Strategies / 三略]] — A classical Chinese military treatise divided into three volumes (Upper, Middle, Lower) addressing military command, statecraft, and governance principles.

## Classification

- [[three-dharmas-framework-buddhism|Three Dharmas / 三法 / 三法]] — A Buddhist doctrinal framework classifying all phenomena into three categories: virtue (德), evil (惡), and basis (依), each containing three subcategories.

## Coming-Of-Age

- [[li-ji-guan-yi-meaning-capping-rite|The Meaning of the Capping Rite / 禮記·冠義]] — A classical Confucian text from the Book of Rites explaining the ritual significance of the capping ceremony as the foundation of all ritual propriety and the gateway to adult moral responsibility.

## Comma-Separated

- [[human-nature-is-good|human-nature-is-good]] — Mencius argues that human nature is inherently good, using the sincere grief during mourning rituals as evidence that moral cultivation through education can develop this innate goodness.
- [[shang-tong-upward-uniformity-mozi|shang-tong-upward-uniformity-mozi]] — This article explains Mozi's "Shang Tong Xia" doctrine, which establishes a four-tier hierarchical political system where unity and moral alignment flow downward from family to state to world to heaven, with the key principle that rulers must understand the true situation of their people to properly govern through rewards and punishments.

## Command-System

- [[mozi-siege-commands-hao-ling|Mozi's Siege Commands and Military Orders / 墨子號令]] — This chapter from the Mozi text details the command system, military discipline, spy operations, and organizational protocols for siege defense, emphasizing strict hierarchy and reward-punishment mechanisms.

## Commentaries

- [[lai-zhou-monk-commentary-dacheng-bensheng-xindi-guanjing|Lai Zhou (來舟) / 來舟法師]] — A Qing Dynasty monk who authored a major commentary on the Mahayana Mind-Ground Contemplation Sutra, synthesizing Huayan and Tiantai classification systems.

## Compassion

- [[compassionate-dragon-king-naga|Compassionate Dragon King (慈心龍王) — Buddhist Narrative of Non-Retaliation / 慈心龍王消伏怨害緣起]] — A Jataka tale depicting a dragon king who conquers the golden-winged garuda through loving-kindness and non-retaliation, exemplifying the power of compassion over violence.
- [[non-retaliation-buddhist-teaching|Non-Retaliation in Buddhist Teaching / 不報怨 / 仏教における報復禁止の教え]] — The Buddhist doctrine of abstaining from vengeance and returning harm with harm, exemplified in the story of King Changshou.

## Confucian-Classics

- [[confucian-gender-roles-neize-education|Gender-Specific Education in the Rites / 男女之教]] — Confucian gender-differentiated education practices, with boys learning the Six Arts and girls learning women's affairs for their designated domestic and social roles.
- [[elderly-care-ran-yang-rites-records|Elderly Care (Yang Lao) in the Rites / 養老禮]] — Confucian rites and practices for caring for the elderly, detailing progressive support based on age, from dietary provisions to royal visits.
- [[great-learning-daxue|The Great Learning / 大學]] — A foundational Confucian classic on self-cultivation and the investigation of things, forming part of the Four Books of Confucianism.
- [[lijineize-rites-inner-principles|Inner Regulations (Neize) from the Book of Rites / 禮記內則]] — A Confucian chapter detailing domestic rituals, family conduct, gender-specific education, elderly care, and cooking methods for proper household governance.
- [[sangfu-xiaoji-liji|Sangfu Xiaoji (Minor Records of Mourning Dress) / 喪服小記]] — A chapter from the Book of Rites detailing mourning dress regulations, mourning periods, and ritual protocols for various kinship relationships.

## Confucian-Concepts

- [[ba-yi-ceremonial-dance|Ba Yi (Eight Rows) / 八佾]] — The ceremonial dance of eight rows of eight performers, a symbol of ritual order and social hierarchy in ancient Chinese rites.
- [[confucian-music-yue|Confucian View of Music (Yue) / 儒家的音乐观（乐）]] — Confucian philosophy on the moral and social functions of music in maintaining ritual order and personal cultivation.

## Confucian-Critique

- [[mozi-fayi-standard-law|Mozi's Standard of Law (法儀) / 墨子法儀]] — Mozi argues that all governance requires a standard or model, and that Heaven (天) rather than parents, teachers, or rulers should serve as the ultimate ethical benchmark.
- [[mozi-fei-yue-shang-against-music-upper|Mozi Against Music Part I (非樂上) — Mohist Critique of Music and Governance]] — Mozi's philosophical argument against elaborate music, contending that rulers' expenditure on music harms the people's welfare and disrupts governance, based on the principle of promoting world benefit while eliminating world harm.
- [[mozi-gong-meng-chapter|Mozi - Gong Meng Chapter / 墨子·公孟]] — A philosophical dialogue between Mozi and the Confucian scholar Gong Meng covering debates on proactive moral speech, ritual propriety, fate, and the unity of words and actions.
- [[mozi-jie-zang-frugal-burial|Mozi on Frugal Burial (節葬) / 墨子節葬]] — Mozi's critique of excessive burial practices and prolonged mourning, arguing for simple burials based on the examples of ancient sage kings.
- [[mozi-jie-zang-funeral-simplicity|Mozi's Funeral Simplicity / 墨子節葬思想]] — Mozi's philosophical argument against elaborate funerals and prolonged mourning, advocating simple burial practices based on utilitarian principles.
- [[zhuangzi-fisherman-yu-fu|The Fisherman Chapter (Yu Fu) / 莊子·漁父]] — A Zhuangzi chapter featuring a Daoist fisherman who teaches Confucius about authenticity (真), criticizing artificial ritual and social conventions while advocating naturalness and genuine sincerity.

## Confucian-Cultivation

- [[knowing-destiny-rites-words|Knowing Destiny, Rites, and Words / 知命知礼知言]] — Confucius's three essential knowledges for becoming a true gentleman in the Analects
- [[mengzi-haoran-qi-vast-flowing-vital-energy|Vast Flowing Qi (浩然之氣) / 浩然之氣]] — Mencius's concept of moral cultivated vital energy that fills the universe when properly nurtured through accumulated righteousness.

## Confucian-Daoist-Dialogue

- [[xinzhai-heart-fasting|Heart Fasting / 心齋]] — A Zhuangzi concept of spiritual purification through emptiness of the heart-mind, taught by Confucius to Yan Hui as the path to navigate the human world.

## Confucian-Daoist-Synthesis

- [[confucius-western-saint-liezi|Confucius and the Western Saint (西方聖者) / 西方聖者]] — A Liezi account of Confucius making an enigmatic reference to "a saint in the west" who rules without governing, speaks without persuasion, and transforms without coercion.
- [[understanding-heaven-knowing-fate-liezi|Understanding Heaven and Knowing Fate (樂天知命) / 樂天知命]] — A Liezi philosophical concept about rejoicing in Heaven's will and knowing one's fate, evolving from conventional wisdom to transcendent understanding.
