## Spiritual-Practice

- [[initial-awakening|Initial Awakening / 初發心 / 初発の覚醒]] — An early stage of spiritual realization in Buddhist practice, marking the first awakening on the path to liberation.
- [[king-mu-spiritual-flight-liezi|King Mu's Spiritual Flight / 周穆王神遊 / 周穆王のspirit journey]] — The philosophical discourse on spiritual transcendence as described in the Liezi account of King Mu's journey with the transformed person.
- [[ultimate-wandering-observation-liezi|Ultimate Wandering and Observation (至游至觀) / 至游至觀]] — A Liezi philosophical concept about the highest form of spiritual wandering and observation, transcending attachment to external objects.

## Spiritual-Training

- [[ji-shengzi-fighting-roosters-liezi|Ji Shengzi's Fighting Roosters: Spiritual Mastery / 紀渻子養鬭雞 — 精神修養之道]] — The story of Ji Shengzi cultivating fighting roosters illustrates the Daoist path to spiritual mastery through the progression from false confidence to true tranquility.

## Spring-And-Autumn-Period

- [[mozi-rejecting-confucians-fei-ru|Mozi's Rejection of Confucians (非儒下) / 墨子·非儒下]] — A Mohist critique of Confucian ethics, mourning rituals, fatalism, and Confucius's political conduct through detailed arguments and historical anecdotes.

## Stages-Of-Awakening

- [[initial-awakening|Initial Awakening / 初發心 / 初発の覚醒]] — An early stage of spiritual realization in Buddhist practice, marking the first awakening on the path to liberation.

## Stages-Of-Practice

- [[arhat-stages-buddhist-liberation|阿羅漢位 / Stages of Arhat Liberation]] — The systematic classification of Buddhist liberation stages from stream-enterer to fully accomplished arhat, as presented in classical Indian Buddhist texts.

## Standard-Of-Law

- [[mozi-fayi-standard-law|Mozi's Standard of Law (法儀) / 墨子法儀]] — Mozi argues that all governance requires a standard or model, and that Heaven (天) rather than parents, teachers, or rulers should serve as the ultimate ethical benchmark.

## State-Building

- [[lai-min-attracting-people|Attracting People Policy (徠民) / 徠民政策]] — Shang Yang's policy to attract settlers from other states to cultivate Qin's wastelands, addressing population scarcity through land incentives.

## State-Craft

- [[first-principle-shangjun-shu|First Principle (壹言) / 壹言]] — A foundational concept from the Book of Lord Shang emphasizing the unity of state power and the importance of concentrating national effort on agriculture and military affairs.
- [[mozi-seven-calamities-qi-huan|Seven Calamities in Mozi / 墨子七患]] — A Mohist analysis of the seven types of calamities that threaten state survival, emphasizing preparedness, agricultural foundation, and virtuous governance.

## State-Governance

- [[three-unifications-legalism-yi-shang-yi-xing-yi-jiao|Three Unifications in Legalism / 壹賞壹刑壹教]] — Lord Shang's doctrine of unified rewards, unified punishment, and unified teaching as the three pillars of Legalist state governance.

## State-Power

- [[nong-zhan-agricultural-war|Agricultural War Doctrine / 農戰]] — A Legalist doctrine from the Book of Lord Shang emphasizing the unification of agricultural production and military service as the twin pillars of state power.
- [[ruo-min-weakening-the-people|Weakening the People (弱民) / 弱民]] — A Legalist political doctrine advocating that rulers should deliberately weaken the populace to strengthen state power, creating dependence through poverty and labor.

## Statecraft

- [[agricultural-foundation|Agricultural Foundation / 农本思想]] — Mencius's governance principle that agricultural development is fundamental to state prosperity
- [[ding-fen-determining-names-positions|Determining Names and Positions (定分) / 定分]] — The Shang Yang doctrine establishing clear legal definitions of social roles and property rights as the foundation for orderly governance and the prevention of social chaos.
- [[five-categories-people-wumin-shangjunshu|Five Categories of People / 五民]] — The Five Categories (五民) refers to Lord Shang's classification of social groups—scholars, hermits, warriors, artisans, and merchants—with their respective roles and governance implications.
- [[mozi-seven-calamities-qi-huan|Seven Calamities in Mozi / 墨子七患]] — A Mohist analysis of the seven types of calamities that threaten state survival, emphasizing preparedness, agricultural foundation, and virtuous governance.
- [[ruo-min-weakening-the-people|Weakening the People (弱民) / 弱民]] — A Legalist political doctrine advocating that rulers should deliberately weaken the populace to strengthen state power, creating dependence through poverty and labor.
- [[three-vermin-three-shixing-shangjunshu|Three Vermin / 三蝨]] — The Three Vermin (三蝨) concept from the Book of Lord Shang describes three parasitic forces that weaken a state: poverty, wealth, and moral corruption.

## Stillness

- [[guarding-stillness-wenzi-jing|Guarding Stillness (守靜) in Wenzi / 文子"守靜"論]] — Guarding Stillness (守靜) in Wenzi Volume 3 presents stillness as the fundamental governance principle, contrasting it with chaos caused by movement, and emphasizing its role in preserving spiritual energy and achieving longevity.

## Strategic-Thinking

- [[tian-shi-di-li-ren-he|Tian Shi Bu Ru Di Li, Di Li Bu Ru Ren He / 天時不如地利，地利不如人和]] — The Mencian doctrine that favorable timing is less important than geographical advantage, which is less important than human harmony.

## Stream-Enterer

- [[arhat-stages-buddhist-liberation|阿羅漢位 / Stages of Arhat Liberation]] — The systematic classification of Buddhist liberation stages from stream-enterer to fully accomplished arhat, as presented in classical Indian Buddhist texts.

## Stream-Entry

- [[bimbisara-king-magadha-ren-xian|King Bimbisara / 頻婆娑羅王]] — The Magadha king devoted to the Buddha, whose past life as a "Human Immortal" attained stream-entry, now reborn as a celestial prince.

## Strength

- [[gong-yibo-strength-liezi|Gong Yibo's Humility About Strength (公儀伯之力) / 公儀伯之力]] — A Liezi anecdote about Gong Yibo explaining true strength through the example of his master Shang Qiu, who possessed invincible power yet never used it.

## Stupa

- [[bodhisattva-throw-body-feed-tiger-stupa-fasheng|The Sutra of Bodhisattva Throwing His Body to Feed the Hungry Tiger and the Stupa's Origin / 菩薩投身餧餓虎起塔因緣經]] — A Buddhist sutra describing Prince Chandana's self-sacrifice to feed seven hungry tiger cubs, the subsequent stupa's miraculous healing powers, and its translator Fasheng of Northern Liang Gaochang.

- [[sun-tzu-art-of-war|Sun Tzu's Art of War / 孫子兵法 / 孫氏兵法]] — An ancient Chinese military treatise by Sun Tzu consisting of thirteen chapters covering strategic principles, tactics, intelligence gathering, and the philosophy of warfare.

## Supernatural-Power

- [[shangqiu-kai-faith-moves-heaven-earth-liezi|Shangqiu Kai: Faith That Moves Heaven and Earth / 商丘開：至信感人]] — The story of Shangqiu Kai demonstrates how supreme sincerity (至信) can move heaven and earth, allowing one to walk through fire without harm.

## Supernatural-Powers

- [[brahma-fourfold-teaching|Brahma's Fourfold Teaching on Liberation / 梵天王四法]] — Mahābrahmā's teachings on the four conditions for rebirth in the Brahma realm: non-self practice, one-pointedness of mind, compassionate liberation, and abandoning defilements.
- [[four-bases-supernatural-power-siddhartha|Four Bases of Supernatural Power / 四神足]] — The Four Bases of Supernatural Power (rddhipāda) taught by Mahabrahma Deva, describing the spiritual faculties of desire, endeavor, mind, and investigation.

- [[mozi-siege-defense-inventory|Mozi's Siege Defense Inventory Standards / 墨子守城物資儲備法]] — Standardized material requirements for city defense including provisions, weapons, and strategic supplies in Mozi's defensive doctrine.

## Survival

- [[cai-yu-bu-cai-zhi-jian|Between Being Useful and Useless / 材與不材之間]] — A Zhuangzi philosophy on navigating between utility and uselessness through alignment with the Dao, avoiding the pitfalls of both extremes.

## Survival-Wisdom

- [[shan-mu-yi-dai-niao|The Yi Dai Bird / 意怠鳥]] — The story of the humble, non-competitive Yi Dai bird in Zhuangzi's Mountain Trees chapter, illustrating the Daoist path of safety through humility and non-distinction.
- [[zhili-qixing-deformed-ones-zhuangzi|The Deformed Ones / 支離其形]] — Zhuangzi's celebration of physically deformed individuals who, excluded from worldly usefulness, survive and prosper—the paradox of form versus spirit in Daoist philosophy.

## Sutra

- [[changahan-jing|Chang Ahan Jing (Long Discourses of the Buddha) / 長阿含經]] — The Dīrgha-āgama, the longest collection of the Buddha's long discourses in early Buddhist scripture, compiled in four sections and five recitations.

## Sutra-Classification

- [[three-treasuries-four-collections|三藏三分 Four Āgamas / Tripartite Canon and Quadruple Sūtra Collections]] — The organization of the Buddhist canon into three treasures and four sūtra collections, attributed to Ānanda's compilation guided by celestial beings.

## Sutra-Commentary

- [[dacheng-bensheng-xindi-guanjing-kewen|大乘本生心地觀經淺註科文 / Commentary Outline on the Mahayana Mind-Ground Contemplation Sutra]] — A comprehensive structural outline and commentary classifying the contents of the Mahayana Sutra of Mind-Ground Contemplation into prefaces, main text, and circulation sections with detailed doctrinal divisions.

## Sutra-Compilation

- [[ananda-compiled-scriptures|阿難集經 Ānanda's Compilation of the Buddhist Canon]] — The Buddha's attendant who compiled the sutras after the Buddha's parinirvana, organizing them into the three treasures and four collections.

- [[ba-en-pin|Ba-en-pin / 报答父母恩品]] — A genre of Chinese Buddhist literature focusing on repaying parental kindness through spiritual practice.

## Sutras

- [[bihuajing|The "Sad Flower Sutra" / 《悲華經》]] — The "Sad Flower Sutra" is a Mahayana Buddhist text encompassing teachings delivered by the Buddha on various profound subjects.
- [[human-immortal-ren-xian|Human Immortal / 人仙]] — A celestial being who is the son of Vaisravana (毘沙門天王) and serves as a messenger revealing the karmic fate of King Bimbisara.

- [[hubin-wheelmaking-discourse-zhuangzi|Wheelwright's Wheel-Making Discourse / 輪扁斲輪]] — A philosophical discourse in Zhuangzi where a wheelwright explains to Duke Huan why the words of the sages are merely "dregs" and true wisdom cannot be transmitted through language.

## Talismans

- [[baopuzi-volume-17-mountain-entry|Baopuzi Volume 17: Mountain Entry Arts / 抱朴子卷十七：入山之法]] — Ge Hong's comprehensive guide to Daoist mountain entry practices, including timing, purification rituals, protective talismans, and methods for dealing with mountain spirits and dangerous creatures.
- [[baopuzi-volume-19-daoist-scriptures-catalog|Baopuzi Volume 19: Catalog of Daoist Texts / 抱朴子卷十九道書目錄]] — Ge Hong's comprehensive catalog of over 180 Daoist texts including Three Sovereigns Inner Text, Five Peaks True Form Map, talismans, alchemy scripts, and esoteric practices, as recorded from his teacher Zheng Jun.
- [[five-peaks-true-form-map-wuyue-zhenxing-tu|Five Peaks True Form Map / 五嶽真形圖]] — A most sacred Taoist talisman text described in Baopuzi as requiring blood oaths, forty-year transmission cycles, and possessing powers to ward off evil, heal diseases, cross waters, and reveal hidden knowledge.

## Tang-Buddhism

- [[miaose-wang-bodhisattva-sacrifice|King Subhūti / 妙色王]] — A past incarnation of the Buddha who sacrificed his son, wife, and body to obtain the Dharma teaching on attachment.

## Tang-Dynasty

- [[da-cheng-li-wen-zi-pu-guang-ming-zang-jing|Mahāyāna Sutra of Universal Light Treasury Transcending Words / 大乘離文字普光明藏經]] — A Mahāyāna Buddhist sutra translated by Divākara during the Tang Dynasty, teaching what bodhisattvas should abandon and realize.

## Tang-Dynasty-Buddhism

- [[da-cheng-li-wen-zi-pu-guang-ming-zang-jing|Mahāyāna Sutra of Universal Light Treasury Transcending Words / 大乘離文字普光明藏經]] — A Mahāyāna Buddhist sutra translated by Divākara during the Tang Dynasty, teaching what bodhisattvas should abandon and realize.
- [[shi-men-tong-pan|十門通判 / Ten-Fold Framework for Sutra Exposition]] — A systematic ten-category methodology for analyzing and expounding Buddhist sutras, originating with Xianshou Fazang and elaborated by later masters.
- [[xianshou-wu-jiao|賢首五教 / Five Teachings of Xianshou / 賢首五教（けんじゅぎょう）]] — A five-tiered doctrinal classification system developed by Fazang (Xianshou) of the Huayan school, categorizing all Buddhist teachings from Hinayana to the highest Yogacara-Tathagatagarbha doctrines.

## Tang-Dynasty-Translations

- [[da-cheng-ben-sheng-xin-di-guan-jing|大乘本生心地觀經 / Mahāyāna Sūtra on the Cultivation of the Mind-Ground]] — A major Mahāyāna Buddhist sutra translated into Chinese during the Tang dynasty, teaching the cultivation of the mind-ground and repaying the four kinds of kindness.
- [[shizi-sutuo-suowa-wang-duanrou-jing|Sutra of King Siṃha-Sūdaśa on Abstaining from Meat / 師子素馱娑王斷肉經]] — A Buddhist sutra recounting how King Siṃha-Sūdaśa, born with a lion's head due to past meat-eating karma, is converted to vegetarianism and non-killing by King Wen Yue through teachings on impermanence and compassion.

## Tang-Translations

- [[miaose-wang-yinyuan-jing|King Subhūti's Cause and Conditions Sutra / 妙色王因緣經]] — A Buddhist sutra depicting King Subhūti's supreme sacrifice of his son, wife, and body to obtain the Dharma teaching on attachment.

## Tang-Wan-Kung

- [[tang-wan-kung|Tang Wan Kung / 唐宓公]] — Overview of the historical and philosophical significance of Tang Wan Kung in Confucianism.

## Taoism

- [[baopuzi-selecting-daoist-texts|On Selecting Daoist Texts in Baopuzi / 抱朴子論道書之選擇]] — Ge Hong's critical assessment of various Daoist texts including the Daodejing and Zhuangzi, arguing that most are incomplete or misleading, and that true cultivation requires proper guidance rather than mere textual study.
- [[dao-the-way-taoism|Dao (The Way) / 道]] — The fundamental Taoist concept of Dao (The Way), the ultimate reality and principle underlying the universe.
- [[de-yi-wang-yan-zhuangzi|Forget the Words When the Meaning is Understood / 得意忘言]] — Zhuangzi's philosophical principle that true understanding transcends language, illustrated through the fish trap and rabbit snare metaphors.
- [[dongmen-wu-grieflessness|Dongmen Wu's Grieflessness / 東門吳之無憂]] — The story of Dongmen Wu, who remained unmoved by his son's death because he had previously been without a son and felt no loss.
- [[force-fate-debate-liezi|Force and Fate Debate / 力命之辯]] — The philosophical dialogue between Force (力) and Fate (命) exploring whether human effort or destiny determines life outcomes.
- [[guan-bao-friendship-liezi|Guan Zhong and Bao Shuya Friendship / 管鮑之交]] — The paradigmatic friendship between Guan Zhong and Bao Shuya, reinterpreted by Liezi as an example of fate determining social outcomes rather than personal virtue.
- [[guanyinzi-chapter-nine|Guanyinzi Chapter Nine: On Medicine / 關尹子第九章：藥者雜治]] — Chapter 9 of Guanyinzi presents the "medicine" metaphor for spiritual practice, discussing how the sage applies various remedies to correct imbalances between extremes.
- [[jing-shen-hun-po-essence-spirit-soul|Essence, Spirit, Soul, and Corporeal Soul (精神魂魄) / 精神魂魄說]] — A Taoist doctrine from Guanyinzi Chapter 4 explaining the four fundamental spiritual faculties: essence (精), spirit (神), soul (魂), and corporeal soul (魄), their cosmic origins, and their relationship to the Five Elements.
- [[king-mu-spiritual-flight-liezi|King Mu's Spiritual Flight / 周穆王神遊 / 周穆王のspirit journey]] — The philosophical discourse on spiritual transcendence as described in the Liezi account of King Mu's journey with the transformed person.
- [[liang-zuo-shan-two-mountains-immortality-baopuzi|Two Mountains of Immortality in Baopuzi / 抱朴子所述兩座仙山]] — A unique esoteric teaching from Baopuzi describing two mystical mountains where immortality can be obtained through proper cultivation.
- [[self-generating-life-death|Self-Generating Life and Death / 自生自死]] — The Liezi doctrine that life, death, prosperity, and poverty arise spontaneously from fate, not from human control.
- [[tai-xi-embryo-breathing-baopuzi|Embryo Breathing (胎息) in Baopuzi / 抱朴子中的胎息之法]] — A detailed examination of the embryo breathing technique (胎息) described in Baopuzi as the supreme method of qi cultivation, enabling practitioners to breathe without using nose or mouth as if in the womb.
- [[wu-yuan-five-origins-guan-yin-zi|The Five Origins (五元) in Guān Yǐnzǐ / 關尹子五元論]] — An exploration of the Five Origins cosmology (天、命、神、元、道) presented in Guān Yǐnzǐ, a Taoist text emphasizing the omnipresence and indivisibility of the cosmic principles.
- [[zhuangzi-daozhi-chapter|Robber Zhi Chapter (盜跖) / 盜跖篇]] — Zhuangzi Chapter 29 presents a fictional dialogue between Confucius and Robber Zhi, featuring radical critiques of Confucian morality, civilization, and social order.

## Taoist-Alchemy

- [[baopuzi-jiu-dan-nine-elixirs|Nine Elixirs in Baopuzi / 抱朴子九丹]] — Baopuzi Volume 4 details the Nine Elixirs (九丹) — the supreme alchemical formulas for immortality including the Cinnabar Flower, Divine Elixir, Return Elixir, and Cold Elixir, along with the Great Clarity Elixir and Golden Liquid methods.

## Taoist-Metaphysics

- [[laochengzi-illusion-transformation-liezi|Lao Chengzi's Study of Illusion / 老成子學幻 / 老成子の幻化学]] — The philosophical narrative of Lao Chengzi learning the art of transformation and illusion from Yin Wen, including the Daoist theory of change and the nature of reality.

## Taoist-Philosophy

- [[bian-shi-wei-zhi|Transforming Knowledge into Wisdom / 變識為智]] — The Daoist philosophical concept of transforming rigid consciousness (識) into flexible wisdom (智), a key theme in Guanyinzi Chapter 5.
- [[guanyinzi-chapter-five-mind-transformation|Guanyinzi Chapter Five: Mind and Cosmological Transformation / 關尹子第五章：心與造化]] — Chapter 5 of Guanyinzi explores the nature of the mind (心), its interactions with spirits and external objects, and the sage's mastery over mental transformation to transcend form and qi.
- [[yi-wei-shi-wo-yi-yi-wei-xin-yi|Intention as Dust, Mind as Transitory / 意者塵往來爾]] — The philosophical concept from Guanyinzi that intention (意) is merely the comings and goings of dust, while the mind (心) remains fundamentally unchanged.

## Taoist-Psychology

- [[eight-testings-six-omens-liezi|Eight Testings and Six Omens / 覺有八徵夢有六候 / 八徵と六候]] — The Liezi philosophical framework classifying eight experiential states of waking life and six categories of dreams, with implications for understanding consciousness.

## Taoist-Texts

- [[baopuzi-selecting-daoist-texts|On Selecting Daoist Texts in Baopuzi / 抱朴子論道書之選擇]] — Ge Hong's critical assessment of various Daoist texts including the Daodejing and Zhuangzi, arguing that most are incomplete or misleading, and that true cultivation requires proper guidance rather than mere textual study.
- [[five-peaks-true-form-map-wuyue-zhenxing-tu|Five Peaks True Form Map / 五嶽真形圖]] — A most sacred Taoist talisman text described in Baopuzi as requiring blood oaths, forty-year transmission cycles, and possessing powers to ward off evil, heal diseases, cross waters, and reveal hidden knowledge.
- [[guan-yinzi-chapter-three-sage-way|Guān Yǐnzǐ Chapter Three: The Way of the Sage / 關尹子第三章：聖人之道]] — Chapter 3 of the Daoist classic Guān Yǐnzǐ explores the sage's governance through non-action, the doctrine of non-self, and the inexpressibility of the Dao.

## Tathagata

- [[dacheng-xindi-guanjing-san-shen|如來三身 / Three Bodies of the Tathagata (三身說)]] — The doctrinal classification of the Buddha's three bodies—Dharma-body, Enjoyment-body, and Transformational body—as expounded in the Mahayana Mind-Ground Contemplation Sutra, with detailed elaboration of their characteristics and salvific functions.
- [[lotus-up-tathagata|蓮華上如來 / Lotus-Up Tathāgata (Liánhuá Shàng Rúlái)]] — A celestial Buddha in Mahāyāna Buddhism who appears in the Lotus World, achieving enlightenment in a single night and manifesting great supernatural powers.
- [[tathagata-eight-rare-qualities|Eight Rare Qualities of a Tathagata / 如來八希有法]] — Eight exceptional qualities that appear when a Buddha enters the world, as taught by Indra and repeated by Brahma, forming a unique doctrinal teaching of this sutra.

## Tathagata-Eight-Rare-Qualities

- [[thirty-three-heavens|Trayastriṃśa Heaven / 三十三天（忉利天）]] — The Heaven of Thirty-Three Gods where the initial discourse of the Great Firm Brāhmaṇa Sūtra takes place, presided over by Śakra (帝釋天主) and the site of the first teaching of the eight rare qualities.

## Tathagata-Origin

- [[void-seal-bodhisattva|虛空印菩薩 / Void Seal Bodhisattva (Xūkōng Yìn Púsà)]] — A bodhisattva in Mahāyāna Buddhism who received the teaching of all-knowledge dhāraṇī and later became the Lotus-Up Tathāgata in the Lotus World.

- [[erya-classic-chinese-glossary|Erya (Classic of Correct Rhymes) / 爾雅]] — The Erya is China's oldest comprehensive glossary, compiled during the Warring States-Han period, providing definitions of classical terms across categories with phonetic annotations.

## Thirty-Seven-Factors

- [[five-roots-five-powers-an-shigao-commentary|Five Roots and Five Powers / 五根五力]] — The Five Roots (信進念定慧) and Five Powers (信力精進力念力定力慧力) as expounded in An Shigao's Han Dynasty Buddhist commentary.

## Thirty-Three-Heavens

- [[brahma-fourfold-teaching|Brahma's Fourfold Teaching on Liberation / 梵天王四法]] — Mahābrahmā's teachings on the four conditions for rebirth in the Brahma realm: non-self practice, one-pointedness of mind, compassionate liberation, and abandoning defilements.
- [[ding-sheng-wang-king-caitanya-dhrtarastra|King Ding Sheng (Ding Sheng Wang) / 頂生王]] — King Ding Sheng is a bodhisattva incarnation who was born from his father's crown, practiced generous giving, conquered the four continents, and ascended through the thirty-three heavens, illustrating Buddhist teachings on merit and the dangers of greed.
- [[ding-sheng-wang-king-mahadyuti-origin-karma|King Ding Sheng (Mahādyuti) — Birth from the Crown and Karmic Journey / 頂生王因緣經 — 頂上化生之因緣敘事]] — A Buddhist Jataka-style narrative recounting how King Mahādyuti, born from his father's crown, conquers the four continents and ascends to Trayastriṃśa Heaven through accumulated merit.
- [[great-brahma-king|Great Brahma King / 大梵天王]] — A celestial deity in Buddhist cosmology who taught the Four Bases of Supernatural Power at the Thirty-three Heavens.
- [[great-firm-brahmin-origin-sutra|Great Firm Brahmin Origin Sutra / 大堅固婆羅門緣起經]] — A Buddhist sutra recounting how the Buddha's past life as Minister Great Firm became enlightened through teachings from the Great Brahma King, then led thousands to liberation across celestial realms.
- [[thirty-three-heavens|Trayastriṃśa Heaven / 三十三天（忉利天）]] — The Heaven of Thirty-Three Gods where the initial discourse of the Great Firm Brāhmaṇa Sūtra takes place, presided over by Śakra (帝釋天主) and the site of the first teaching of the eight rare qualities.

## Thirty‑Seven Bodhiparamitas

- [[七覺意注-(安世高)|Seven Factors of Enlightenment Commentary (An Shigao) / 七覺意注（安世高）]] — An early Chinese commentary by An Shigao on the seven factors of enlightenment within the thirty‑seven bodhiparamitas.

## Thirty‑Seven Bodhipāramitās

- [[五根五力注-(安世高)|Five Roots and Five Powers Commentary (An Shigao) / 五根五力注 (安世高)]] — Commentary on the Five Roots and Five Powers by the early Chinese Buddhist translator An Shigao, forming part of the systematic exposition of the thirty‑seven bodhipāramitās.

## Thousand-Lamps

- [[thousand-lamp-body-offering-bodhisattva-practice|The King Who Lit a Thousand Lamps / 以身燃千燈之王]] — The Buddhist narrative of a king who sacrificed his own flesh to light a thousand lamps as the ultimate act of dedication to the Dharma.

## Three Poisons

- [[three-poisons-greed-hatred-delusion-buddhist-teaching|三毒的業報與解脫之道 / 三毒的業報與解脫之道 / 三毒の業報と解脱への道]] — Buddhist teachings on the three poisons (贪瞋痴) and their role in binding beings to samsara, as illustrated through multiple narratives in the Shengjing.

## Three-Bodies-Doctrine

- [[dacheng-xindi-guanjing-san-shen|如來三身 / Three Bodies of the Tathagata (三身說)]] — The doctrinal classification of the Buddha's three bodies—Dharma-body, Enjoyment-body, and Transformational body—as expounded in the Mahayana Mind-Ground Contemplation Sutra, with detailed elaboration of their characteristics and salvific functions.

## Three-Dharmas

- [[evil-section-three-dharmas-sanfang-dunlun|Evil Section (惡品) in the Three Dharmas Treatise / 三法度論惡品]] — The second chapter of the Three Dharmas Treatise examining evil deeds, desire, and delusion as the three unwholesome roots.
- [[four-agamas-commentary-commentary-on-four-collections|Four Āgamas Commentary / 四阿鋡暮抄解]] — A Buddhist philosophical commentary on the Four Āgamas discussing the Three Dharmas of merit, evil, and liberation.
- [[three-dharmas-buddhist-philosophy|Three Dharmas / 三法]] — A fundamental Buddhist philosophical framework comprising merit, evil, and liberation through dependent awakening.
- [[three-dharmas-framework-buddhism|Three Dharmas / 三法 / 三法]] — A Buddhist doctrinal framework classifying all phenomena into three categories: virtue (德), evil (惡), and basis (依), each containing three subcategories.
- [[three-types-liberation-buddhist-uppsala|Three Types of Liberation in Buddhist Practice / 佛教三種解脫]] — The classification of liberation into desire liberation, form liberation, and cessation absorption, as discussed in the Three Dharmas Treatise.
- [[upaya-skillful-means-three-dharmas|Skillful Means (方便) in the Three Dharmas Treatise / 三法度論方便]] — The concept of skillful means (upāya) as the path leading to liberation, comprising precepts, concentration, and wisdom.

## Three-Foundations

- [[shang-xian-middle-mozi|Shang Xian Zhong (Exalting the Worthy, Part 2) / 尚賢中]] — The second chapter of Mozi's Exalting the Worthy doctrine, presenting the "Three Foundations" theory and historical exemplars of sage kings who achieved governance through elevating worthy ministers.

## Three-Jewels

- [[great-firm-brahman-backstory|The Origin Story of the Great Firm Brāhmaṇa / 大堅固婆羅門緣起]] — A Buddhist sūtra recounting how King Linu's minister Mahākakuda meets the Buddha, attains stream-entry, renounces worldly life, and becomes an arhat, inspiring seven kings, seven thousand brāhmaṇas, and countless laypeople to follow the Dharma.

## Three-Poisons

- [[evil-classification-buddhism-e|Evil and Unwholesome Qualities / 惡 / 悪]] — Buddhist classification of unwholesome qualities including bodily, verbal, and mental misconduct, arising from the three poisons.

## Three-Refuges

- [[three-treasures|Three Treasures / 三宝]] — The three foundational refuges of Buddhism—Buddha, Dharma, and Sangha—considered precious objects of veneration and sources of spiritual refuge.

## Three-Roots

- [[virtue-merit-buddhism-de|Merit and Virtue in Buddhist Practice / 德 / 徳]] — Buddhist concept of merit (德, puṇya) encompassing giving, morality, meditation, and the three roots of wholesome qualities.

## Three-Roots-Goodness

- [[virtue-merit-buddhist-doctrine-de-pin|Virtue Section (德品) - Buddhist Spiritual Cultivation]] — The first section of the Three Dharmas Treatise detailing the cultivation of merit, roots of goodness, and non-evil qualities.

## Three-Treasures

- [[tai-xi-embryo-breathing-baopuzi|Embryo Breathing (胎息) in Baopuzi / 抱朴子中的胎息之法]] — A detailed examination of the embryo breathing technique (胎息) described in Baopuzi as the supreme method of qi cultivation, enabling practitioners to breathe without using nose or mouth as if in the womb.

## Three-Treasuries

- [[ananda-compiled-scriptures|阿難集經 Ānanda's Compilation of the Buddhist Canon]] — The Buddha's attendant who compiled the sutras after the Buddha's parinirvana, organizing them into the three treasures and four collections.
- [[ten-remembrances-buddhist-meditation|Ten Remembrances / 十念]] — A Buddhist meditation practice involving ten objects of mindfulness, from the Commentary on Classifying Merit.
- [[three-treasuries-four-collections|三藏三分 Four Āgamas / Tripartite Canon and Quadruple Sūtra Collections]] — The organization of the Buddhist canon into three treasures and four sūtra collections, attributed to Ānanda's compilation guided by celestial beings.

## Three-Years-Mourning

- [[three-years-mourning|Three Years Mourning / 三年之丧]] — The traditional mourning period of three years emphasizes filial piety and respect for deceased parents.

## Threeworms

- [[three-vermin-three-shixing-shangjunshu|Three Vermin / 三蝨]] — The Three Vermin (三蝨) concept from the Book of Lord Shang describes three parasitic forces that weaken a state: poverty, wealth, and moral corruption.

## Tian-Jun

- [[zhuangzi-fables-parables-yuyan|Zhuangzi Chapter 27: Fables / 莊子·寓言]] — The 27th chapter of Zhuangzi introducing three types of discourse—fables, elders' sayings, and spontaneous speech—to convey Daoist teachings through external examples and natural patterns.

## Tian-Ni

- [[zhuangzi-fables-parables-yuyan|Zhuangzi Chapter 27: Fables / 莊子·寓言]] — The 27th chapter of Zhuangzi introducing three types of discourse—fables, elders' sayings, and spontaneous speech—to convey Daoist teachings through external examples and natural patterns.

## Tianrui

- [[four-stages-life-liezi-tianrui|Four Stages of Life in Liezi's Tianrui Chapter / 列子天瑞四階段人生觀]] — An analysis of Liezi's philosophical framework depicting human life through four transformative stages: infancy, youth, old age, and death, each characterized by distinct qi and virtue states.

## Tianzhi

- [[mozi-fayi-standard-law|Mozi's Standard of Law (法儀) / 墨子法儀]] — Mozi argues that all governance requires a standard or model, and that Heaven (天) rather than parents, teachers, or rulers should serve as the ultimate ethical benchmark.

## Time

- [[baopuzi-chapter-14-life-brevity-calculation|Life's Brevity and Urgency in Baopuzi / 抱朴子卷十四：人生短促之歎]] — Ge Hong's vivid calculation of human lifespan, comparing life to a sacrificial animal approaching the slaughterhouse, emphasizing the urgency of cultivation practice.

## Tipitaka

- [[three-treasuries-four-collections|三藏三分 Four Āgamas / Tripartite Canon and Quadruple Sūtra Collections]] — The organization of the Buddhist canon into three treasures and four sūtra collections, attributed to Ānanda's compilation guided by celestial beings.

## Transcendence

- [[baopuzi-immortality-debate|Bao Puzi on Immortals / 抱朴子论神仙不死]] — Ge Hong's philosophical defense of immortality through natural transformation and historical evidence.
- [[guanyinzi-chapter-eight|Guanyinzi Chapter 8 / 關尹子第八篇]] — Chapter 8 of the Daoist text Guanyinzi discusses the ineffable nature of the Dao, the five-element transformations, the heart-mind as creator of all things, and the sage's unity with Heaven.
- [[king-mu-spiritual-flight-liezi|King Mu's Spiritual Flight / 周穆王神遊 / 周穆王のspirit journey]] — The philosophical discourse on spiritual transcendence as described in the Liezi account of King Mu's journey with the transformed person.

## Transformation

- [[five-elements-theory-constancy-transformation|Five Elements Theory: Constancy and Transformation / 五行常變論]] — The theory of five elements (water, fire, wood, metal, earth) as constant yet infinitely variable principles in Chinese cosmology and philosophy.
- [[four-stages-life-liezi-tianrui|Four Stages of Life in Liezi's Tianrui Chapter / 列子天瑞四階段人生觀]] — An analysis of Liezi's philosophical framework depicting human life through four transformative stages: infancy, youth, old age, and death, each characterized by distinct qi and virtue states.
- [[guanyinzi-chapter-five-mind-transformation|Guanyinzi Chapter Five: Mind and Cosmological Transformation / 關尹子第五章：心與造化]] — Chapter 5 of Guanyinzi explores the nature of the mind (心), its interactions with spirits and external objects, and the sage's mastery over mental transformation to transcend form and qi.
- [[guanyinzi-chapter-seven-transformation|Chapter Seven: Transformation (化) in Guanyinzi / 關尹子第七章：化]] — Chapter 7 of Guanyinzi explores the philosophy of transformation (化),阐發道化萬物、聖人任化的深層道理.
- [[kun-peng-giant-fish-bird-liezi|Kun and Peng / 鯤鵬]] — The legendary giant fish Kun that transforms into the massive Peng bird, a cosmological concept from Liezi describing the vastness of the universe and the transformation of beings.
- [[laochengzi-illusion-transformation-liezi|Lao Chengzi's Study of Illusion / 老成子學幻 / 老成子の幻化学]] — The philosophical narrative of Lao Chengzi learning the art of transformation and illusion from Yin Wen, including the Daoist theory of change and the nature of reality.
- [[pure-qi-transformation-hunqi-bianhua|Pure Qi Transformation / 純氣變化]] — A Daoist concept from Guanyinzi describing how pure qi (氣) can transform all things in the universe, including reversing natural laws and animating inanimate objects.
- [[transformation-generation-huasheng-liezi|Transformation and Generation (化生) / 化生]] — The Liezi philosophical principle that all things are generated through transformation in an endless cyclical process.

## Translation

- [[bodhisattva-throw-body-feed-tiger-stupa-fasheng|The Sutra of Bodhisattva Throwing His Body to Feed the Hungry Tiger and the Stupa's Origin / 菩薩投身餧餓虎起塔因緣經]] — A Buddhist sutra describing Prince Chandana's self-sacrifice to feed seven hungry tiger cubs, the subsequent stupa's miraculous healing powers, and its translator Fasheng of Northern Liang Gaochang.

## Translation-History

- [[an-shigao-translation-methodology|An Shigao's Translation Methodology / 安世高譯經方法]] — The translation techniques and contribution of An Shigao, the seminal Parthian monk who translated over 90 Buddhist texts into Chinese during the Eastern Han dynasty.
- [[kumarrow-translation-commentary|Kumārajīva's Translation Methodology in Four Āgamas Commentary / 鳩摩羅什譯經方法]] — Documentation of Kumārajīva's translation practices during the Former Qin dynasty, including team translation methods and philological approaches.

## Translation-Works

- [[fa-ju-monk|Fajü (法炬) — Western Jin Buddhist Translator / 法炬]] — Fajü was a Buddhist monk from the Western Jin dynasty who translated multiple sutras including the Sutra of the Three Cycles of Past Lives.

## Trayastriṃśa

- [[thirty-three-heavens|Trayastriṃśa Heaven / 三十三天（忉利天）]] — The Heaven of Thirty-Three Gods where the initial discourse of the Great Firm Brāhmaṇa Sūtra takes place, presided over by Śakra (帝釋天主) and the site of the first teaching of the eight rare qualities.

## Tricycles

- [[brahma-fourfold-teaching|Brahma's Fourfold Teaching on Liberation / 梵天王四法]] — Mahābrahmā's teachings on the four conditions for rebirth in the Brahma realm: non-self practice, one-pointedness of mind, compassionate liberation, and abandoning defilements.

## Trigrams

- [[bagua-formation-trigrams-yijing|Eight Trigrams Formation / 八卦成列]] — The philosophical principle of how the eight trigrams are arranged to manifest all phenomena in the Yijing

## Tripartite-Classification

- [[san-fa-du-lun-three-dharmas-treatise|Three Dharmas Treatise (三法度論)]] — A Buddhist philosophical treatise organized into three sections explaining virtue, evil, and liberation paths.

## Tripartite-Teaching

- [[san-dharmas-upaya-buddhist-classification|Three Dharmas Classification System (三法)]] — A Buddhist doctrinal classification system organizing teachings into virtue, evil, and liberation paths.

## Triyana

- [[dacheng-xindi-guanjing-san-shen|如來三身 / Three Bodies of the Tathagata (三身說)]] — The doctrinal classification of the Buddha's three bodies—Dharma-body, Enjoyment-body, and Transformational body—as expounded in the Mahayana Mind-Ground Contemplation Sutra, with detailed elaboration of their characteristics and salvific functions.

## Tunnel-Warfare

- [[mozi-preparing-against-tunnel-attacks|Preparing Against Tunnel Attacks (Mozi Chapter on Underground Defense) / 墨子備穴]] — A defensive warfare chapter from the Mozi text detailing strategies to detect and counter enemy tunneling attacks under city walls using acoustic detection, smoke熏攻, and structural defenses.
- [[tu-men-tunnel-gates-city-defense|Tumen (Tunnel Gates) / 突門（城門突入口）]] — Tumen were hidden tunnel gate passages built into city walls at intervals of every hundred paces, designed as defensive traps against underground siege attacks using kilns, bellows, and smoke.

## Turtle

- [[turtle-monkey-past-life-karmic-narrative-shengjing|鱉獼猴前世的業報故事 / 鱉と獼猴の前世因果物語 / 거북이와 원숭이의 전생 업보 이야기]] — The turtle and monkey past-life karmic connection in the Shengjing, illustrating how past-life relationships manifest in the present and the consequences of broken trust.

## Twelve-Austerities

- [[toutuo-xing|頭陀行 / Dhutanga Practices]] — 頭陀行乃佛教十三種清淨苦行，修習此法可去衣、食、住之貪著，速得解脫

## Twelve-Links

- [[human-desire-to-be-born-sutra|Sutra on Human Desire to Be Born / 人本欲生經]] — A Buddhist sutra on the twelve links of dependent origination, attributed to An Shigao's translation from the Later Han dynasty.
- [[twelve-links-dependent-origination-an-shigao-commentary|Twelve Links of Dependent Origination / 十二因緣 / 十二縁起]] — Analysis of the twelve links of dependent origination as explained in An Shigao's commentary on the Yin Chi Ru Jing.

## Twelve-Nidanas

- [[twelve-links-dependent-origination-an-shigao-commentary|Twelve Links of Dependent Origination / 十二因緣 / 十二縁起]] — Analysis of the twelve links of dependent origination as explained in An Shigao's commentary on the Yin Chi Ru Jing.

## Unity

- [[mengzi-unity-through-non-killing-ding-yu-yi|Unity Through Non-Killing / 定於一]] — Mencius' doctrine that unity of the realm is achieved through rulers who do not delight in killing.
- [[shang-tong-upper-unity-mozi|Shang Tong (Upper Unity) / 尚同]] — Shang Tong is Mozi's political doctrine advocating hierarchical unity of thought under proper authority to achieve social order.

## Universal-Light-Treasury

- [[da-cheng-li-wen-zi-pu-guang-ming-zang-jing|Mahāyāna Sutra of Universal Light Treasury Transcending Words / 大乘離文字普光明藏經]] — A Mahāyāna Buddhist sutra translated by Divākara during the Tang Dynasty, teaching what bodhisattvas should abandon and realize.

## Universal-Love

- [[bu-xiang-ai|Non-Mutual Love / 不相愛]] — Mozi's concept identifying the lack of mutual love as the fundamental cause of all social chaos and disorder.
- [[mozi-da-qu|Mozi Da Qu (Great Adoption) / 墨子·大取]] — An analysis of the Mozi chapter "Da Qu" which discusses the methodology of moral weighing between benefit and harm, including principles of self-sacrifice for the world.

## Universalism

- [[jian-ai|Universal Love (兼愛) / 兼愛]] — The Mohist principle advocating equal care for all people without distinction, considered the foundation of Mozi's ethical philosophy.

## Unwholesome

- [[evil-classification-buddhism-e|Evil and Unwholesome Qualities / 惡 / 悪]] — Buddhist classification of unwholesome qualities including bodily, verbal, and mental misconduct, arising from the three poisons.

## Unwholesome Roots

- [[three-roots-of-unwholesomeness|Three Roots of Unwholesomeness / 三不善根]] — The three fundamental unwholesome mental roots—greed, hatred, and delusion—that underlie all negative karmic actions in Buddhism.

## Upaya

- [[upaya-expedient-means-buddhism|Expedient Means / 方便 / 方便]] — Buddhist concept of upaya (expedient means) as the practical methods and path structures for achieving spiritual liberation.

## Upāya

- [[compassionate-dragon-king-naga|Compassionate Dragon King (慈心龍王) — Buddhist Narrative of Non-Retaliation / 慈心龍王消伏怨害緣起]] — A Jataka tale depicting a dragon king who conquers the golden-winged garuda through loving-kindness and non-retaliation, exemplifying the power of compassion over violence.

## Usability-Value

- [[wuyong-zhi-yong-usefulness-of-uselessness|The Usefulness of Uselessness / 無用之用]] — A central Zhuangzi parable about the useless tree that survives because it has no use to humans, illustrating the Daoist principle that apparent uselessness may be the highest utility.

## Utilitarian-Criteria

- [[mozi-practical-standards-utilitarian-criteria|Mozi's Practical Standards for Governance / 墨子實用標準]] — Mozi's criteria for evaluating the utility of clothing, shelter, weapons, and transportation in governance decisions.

## Utilitarian-Ethics

- [[mozi-jie-zang-funeral-simplicity|Mozi's Funeral Simplicity / 墨子節葬思想]] — Mozi's philosophical argument against elaborate funerals and prolonged mourning, advocating simple burial practices based on utilitarian principles.

## Utilitarian-Philosophy

- [[mozi-jie-yong-utility-frugality|Mozi on Utility (節用) — The Principle of Frugality in Mohist Governance / 墨子節用思想——兼愛天下的功利原則]] — Mozi's "On Frugality" (節用) chapter outlines the principle that rulers should only employ resources for practical utility, eliminating wasteful expenditures to maximize social benefit and national strength.

## Utilitarianism

- [[mozi-jie-zang-frugal-burial|Mozi on Frugal Burial (節葬) / 墨子節葬]] — Mozi's critique of excessive burial practices and prolonged mourning, arguing for simple burials based on the examples of ancient sage kings.
- [[mozi-three-debates-music-governance|Mozi's Three Debates on Music and Governance / 墨子三辯]] — A philosophical dialogue in the Mozi examining why sage-kings did not engage in music, and the inverse relationship between musical complexity and governance effectiveness.

## Utility

- [[cai-yu-bu-cai-zhi-jian|Between Being Useful and Useless / 材與不材之間]] — A Zhuangzi philosophy on navigating between utility and uselessness through alignment with the Dao, avoiding the pitfalls of both extremes.

## Utopia

- [[huaxu-dream-liezi|The Huaxu Dream (華胥之夢) / 華胥之夢]] — The Yellow Emperor's dream journey to the utopian land of Huaxu, representing ideal governance and natural harmony.
- [[huaxu-kingdom-liezi|The Huaxu Kingdom / 華胥氏之國]] — The Yellow Emperor's dream of the utopian Huaxu Kingdom and his subsequent enlightened reign, illustrating the Daoist ideal of natural governance through non-action.
- [[jian-de-zhi-guo|Nation of Established Virtue / 建德之國]] — The ideal Daoist society described by Shi Nan Yi Liao in the Zhuangzi—simple, without artificial desires, where people act freely and live and die with peace.

## Vaipulya-Sutra

- [[da-cheng-li-wen-zi-pu-guang-ming-zang-jing|Mahāyāna Sutra of Universal Light Treasury Transcending Words / 大乘離文字普光明藏經]] — A Mahāyāna Buddhist sutra translated by Divākara during the Tang Dynasty, teaching what bodhisattvas should abandon and realize.

## Vaisravana

- [[brahma-fourfold-teaching|Brahma's Fourfold Teaching on Liberation / 梵天王四法]] — Mahābrahmā's teachings on the four conditions for rebirth in the Brahma realm: non-self practice, one-pointedness of mind, compassionate liberation, and abandoning defilements.
- [[human-immortal-sutra-ren-xian-jing|Human Immortal Sutra / 人仙經]] — A Mahayana sutra detailing the Buddha's teaching on the rebirth of King Bimbisara through the celestial being Human Immortal.

## Vasumitra

- [[shizi-yue-fo-ben-sheng-jing|The Lion-Moon Buddha Jataka Sutra / 師子月佛本生經]] — A Buddhist Jataka sutra describing how a monkey who received the Five Precepts from an arhat was reborn over multiple lives and eventually became the Buddha Shi Zi Yue (Lion-Moon), with 84,000 golden monkeys receiving bodhisattva predictions.

## Vegetarianism

- [[shizi-sutuo-suowa-wang-duanrou-jing|Sutra of King Siṃha-Sūdaśa on Abstaining from Meat / 師子素馱娑王斷肉經]] — A Buddhist sutra recounting how King Siṃha-Sūdaśa, born with a lion's head due to past meat-eating karma, is converted to vegetarianism and non-killing by King Wen Yue through teachings on impermanence and compassion.
